style="padding:0 0.1em 0.4em">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/List_of_Major_League_Baseball_postseason_teams" title="List of Major League Baseball postseason teams">Appearances</a></li>\n<li><a style="text-align:right;font-size:115%"><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:MLB_playoffs_sidebar" title="Template:MLB playoffs sidebar"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:MLB_playoffs_sidebar" title="Template talk:MLB playoffs sidebar"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:MLB_playoffs_sidebar&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <b>World Series</b> is the annual championship series of <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a> (MLB) in North America, contested since <a href="/wiki/1903_World_Series" title="1903 World Series">1903</a> between the <a href="/wiki/American_League" title="American League">American League</a> (AL) champion team and the <a href="/wiki/National_League" title="National League">National League</a> (NL) champion team. The winner of the World Series championship is determined through a <a href="/wiki/Best-of-seven_playoff" class="mw-redirect" title="Best-of-seven playoff">best-of-seven playoff</a>, and the winning team is awarded the <a href="/wiki/Commissioner%27s_Trophy_(MLB)" title="Commissioner&#39;s Trophy (MLB)">Commissioner\'s Trophy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> As the series is played during the <a href="/wiki/Autumn" title="Autumn">fall</a> season in North America, it is sometimes referred to as the <b>Fall Classic</b>.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Prior to 1969, the team with the best regular season win-loss record in each league automatically advanced to the World Series; since then each league has conducted a <a href="/wiki/League_Championship_Series" title="League Championship Series">championship series</a> (<a href="/wiki/American_League_Championship_Series" title="American League Championship Series">ALCS</a> and <a href="/wiki/National_League_Championship_Series" title="National League Championship Series">NLCS</a>) preceding the World Series to determine which teams will advance. As of 2017, the World Series has been contested 113 times, with the AL winning 65 and the NL winning 48.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/2017_World_Series" title="2017 World Series">2017 World Series</a> took place between the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Dodgers" title="Los Angeles Dodgers">Los Angeles Dodgers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Houston_Astros" title="Houston Astros">Houston Astros</a>. Seven games were played, with the Astros victorious after game seven, played in Los Angeles. This was the first World Series won by the Astros.\n</p><p>In the American League, the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">New York Yankees</a> have played in 40 World Series and won 27, the <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Philadelphia_Athletics" title="History of the Philadelphia Athletics">Philadelphia</a>/<a href="/wiki/Kansas_City_Athletics" class="mw-redirect" title="Kansas City Athletics">Kansas City</a>/<a href="/wiki/Oakland_Athletics" title="Oakland Athletics">Oakland Athletics</a> have played in 14 and won 9, and the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Red_Sox" title="Boston Red Sox">Boston Red Sox</a> have played in 12 and won 8, including the first World Series. In the National League, the <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Cardinals" title="St. Louis Cardinals">St. Louis Cardinals</a> have appeared in 19 and won 11, the <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_New_York_Giants_(NL)" class="mw-redirect" title="History of the New York Giants (NL)">New York</a>/<a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Giants" title="San Francisco Giants">San Francisco Giants</a> have played in 20 and won 8, the <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Brooklyn_Dodgers" title="History of the Brooklyn Dodgers">Brooklyn</a>/<a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Dodgers" title="Los Angeles Dodgers">Los Angeles Dodgers</a> have appeared in 19 and won 6, and the <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati_Reds" title="Cincinnati Reds">Cincinnati Reds</a> have appeared in 9 and won 5.\n</p><p>As of 2018, no team has won consecutive World Series championships since the New York Yankees in <a href="/wiki/1998_World_Series" title="1998 World Series">1998</a>, <a href="/wiki/1999_World_Series" title="1999 World Series">1999</a>, and <a href="/wiki/2000_World_Series" title="2000 World Series">2000</a>\xe2\x80\x94the longest such drought in Major League Baseball history.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" <span class="toctext">2010s</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-27"><a href="#Modern_World_Series_appearances_by_franchise"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Modern World Series appearances by franchise</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-28"><a href="#World_Series_record_by_team_or_franchise,_1903\xe2\x80\x932017"><span class="tocnumber">3.1</span> <span class="toctext">World Series record by team or franchise, 1903\xe2\x80\x932017</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-29"><a href="#Team_patterns_in_the_World_Series"><span class="tocnumber">3.2</span> <span class="toctext">Team patterns in the World Series</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-30"><a href="#Streaks_and_droughts"><span class="tocnumber">3.2.1</span> <span class="toctext">Streaks and droughts</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-31"><a href="#Game-by-game"><span class="tocnumber">3.2.2</span> <span class="toctext">Game-by-game</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-32"><a href="#Local_rivalries"><span class="tocnumber">3.2.3</span> <span class="toctext">Local rivalries</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-4 tocsection-33"><a href="#Cross-town_Series"><span class="tocnumber">3.2.3.1</span> <span class="toctext">Cross-town Series</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-4 tocsection-34"><a href="#Cross-state_rivalries"><span class="tocnumber">3.2.3.2</span> <span class="toctext">Cross-state rivalries</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-35"><a href="#Pennants_won_in_different_cities"><span class="tocnumber">3.2.4</span> <span class="toctext">Pennants won in different cities</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-36"><a href="#The_original_sixteen_teams"><span class="tocnumber">3.2.5</span> <span class="toctext">The original sixteen teams</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-37"><a href="#Expansion_teams_(after_1960)"><span class="tocnumber">3.2.6</span> <span class="toctext">Expansion teams (after 1960)</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-38"><a href="#Other_notes"><span class="tocnumber">3.2.7</span> <span class="toctext">Other notes</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-39"><a href="#Television_coverage_and_ratings"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Television coverage and ratings</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-40"><a href="#International_participation"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">International participation</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-41"><a href="#Image_gallery"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Image gallery</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-42"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-43"><a href="#Notes"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-44"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-45"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-46"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span id="Precursors_to_the_modern_World_Series_.281857.E2.80.931902.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Precursors_to_the_modern_World_Series_(1857\xe2\x80\x931902)">Precursors to the modern World Series (1857\xe2\x80\x931902)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Precursors to the modern World Series (1857\xe2\x80\x931902)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_pre-World_Series_baseball_champions" title="List of pre-World Series baseball champions">List of pre-World Series baseball champions</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_original_World_Series">The original World Series</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: The original World Series">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Until the formation of the <a href="/wiki/American_Association_(19th_century)" title="American Association (19th century)">American Association</a> in 1882 as a second major league, the <a href="/wiki/National_Association_of_Professional_Base_Ball_Players" title="National Association of Professional Base Ball Players">National Association of Professional Base Ball Players</a> (1871\xe2\x80\x931875) and then the <a href="/wiki/National_League" title="National League">National League</a> (founded 1876) represented the top level of organized baseball in the United States. All championships were awarded to the team with the best record at the end of the season, without a postseason series being played. From 1884 to 1890, the National League and the American Association faced each other in a series of games at the end of the season to determine an overall champion. These series were disorganized in comparison to the modern World Series, with the terms arranged through negotiation of the owners of the championship teams beforehand. The number of games played ranged from as few as three in <a href="/wiki/1884_World_Series" title="1884 World Series">1884</a> (Providence defeated New York three games to zero), to a high of fifteen in <a href="/wiki/1887_World_Series" title="1887 World Series">1887</a> (Detroit beat St. Louis ten games to five). Both the <a href="/wiki/1885_World_Series" title="1885 World Series">1885</a> and <a href="/wiki/1890_World_Series" title="1890 World Series">1890</a> Series ended in ties, each team having won three games with one tie game.<sup id="cite_ref-BR_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BR-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The series was promoted and referred to as "The Championship of the United States",<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> "World\'s Championship Series", or "World\'s Series" for short.\nIn his book <i>Krakatoa: The Day the World Exploded: August 27, 1883</i>, <a href="/wiki/Simon_Winchester" title="Simon Winchester">Simon Winchester</a> mentions in passing that the World Series was named for the <i><a href="/wiki/New_York_World" title="New York World">New York World</a></i> newspaper,<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> but this view is disputed.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The 19th-century competitions are, however, not officially recognized as part of World Series history by <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a>, as it considers 19th-century baseball to be a prologue to the modern baseball era.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Until about 1960, some sources treated the 19th-century Series on an equal basis with the post-19th-century series.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> After about 1930, however, many authorities list the start of the World Series in 1903 and discuss the earlier contests separately.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n(For example, the 1929 <i><a href="/wiki/World_Almanac_and_Book_of_Facts" class="mw-redirect" title="World Almanac and Book of Facts">World Almanac and Book of Facts</a></i> lists "Baseball World\'s Championships 1884\xe2\x80\x931928" in a single table,<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> but the 1943 edition lists "Baseball World Championships 1903\xe2\x80\x931942".<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>)\n</p>\n<h3><span id="1892.E2.80.931900:_.22The_Monopoly_Years.22"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1892\xe2\x80\x931900:_&quot;The_Monopoly_Years&quot;">1892\xe2\x80\x931900: "The Monopoly Years"</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1892\xe2\x80\x931900: &quot;The Monopoly Years&quot;">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Following the collapse of the American Association after the 1891 season, the National League was again the only major league. The league championship was awarded in 1892 by a playoff between half-season champions. This scheme was abandoned after one season.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Beginning in 1893\xe2\x80\x94and continuing until divisional play was introduced in 1969\xe2\x80\x94the pennant was awarded to the first-place club in the standings at the end of the season. For four seasons, 1894\xe2\x80\x931897, the league champions played the runners-up in the post season championship series called the <a href="/wiki/Temple_Cup" title="Temple Cup">Temple Cup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> A second attempt at this format was the <a href="/wiki/Chronicle-Telegraph_Cup" title="Chronicle-Telegraph Cup"><i>Chronicle-Telegraph</i> Cup</a> series, which was played only once, in 1900.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1901, the <a href="/wiki/American_League" title="American League">American League</a> was formed as a second major league. No championship series were played in 1901 or 1902 as the National and American Leagues fought each other for business supremacy (in 1902, the top teams instead opted to <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League_(1902)" title="National Football League (1902)">compete in a <i>football</i> championship</a>).\n</p>\n<h2><span id="Modern_World_Series_.281903.E2.80.93present.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_World_Series_(1903\xe2\x80\x93present)">Modern World Series (1903\xe2\x80\x93present)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Modern World Series (1903\xe2\x80\x93present)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_World_Series_champions" title="List of World Series champions">List of World Series champions</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="First_attempt">First attempt</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: First attempt">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>After two years of bitter competition and player raiding, the National and American Leagues made peace and, as part of the accord, several pairs of teams squared off for interleague exhibition games after the 1903 season. These series were arranged by the participating clubs, as the 1880s World\'s Series matches had been. One of them matched the two pennant winners, <a href="/wiki/1903_Pittsburgh_Pirates_season" title="1903 Pittsburgh Pirates season">Pittsburgh Pirates</a> of the NL and <a href="/wiki/1903_Boston_Americans_season" title="1903 Boston Americans season">Boston Americans</a> (later known as the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Red_Sox" title="Boston Red Sox">Red Sox</a>) of the AL; that one is known as the <a href="/wiki/1903_World_Series" title="1903 World Series">1903 World Series</a>. It had been arranged well in advance by the two owners, as both teams were league leaders by large margins.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Boston upset Pittsburgh by five games to three, winning with pitching depth behind <a href="/wiki/Cy_Young" title="Cy Young">Cy Young</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bill_Dinneen" title="Bill Dinneen">Bill Dinneen</a> and with the support of the band of <a href="/wiki/Royal_Rooters" title="Royal Rooters">Royal Rooters</a>. The Series brought much civic pride to Boston and proved the new American League could beat the Nationals.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Boycott_of_1904">Boycott of 1904</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Boycott of 1904">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=World_Series&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span>  <small><i>(October 2016)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/1904_World_Series" title="1904 World Series">1904 Series</a>, if it had been held, would have been between the AL\'s <a href="/wiki/1904_Boston_Americans_season" title="1904 Boston Americans season">Boston Americans</a> (Boston Red Sox) and the NL\'s <a href="/wiki/1904_New_York_Giants_season" title="1904 New York Giants season">New York Giants</a> (now the <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Giants" title="San Francisco Giants">San Francisco Giants</a>). At that point there was no governing body for the World Series nor any requirement that a Series be played. Thus the Giants\' owner <a href="/wiki/John_T._Brush" title="John T. Brush">John T. Brush</a> refused to allow his team to participate in such an event, citing the "inferiority" of the upstart American League. <a href="/wiki/John_McGraw_(baseball)" class="mw-redirect" title="John McGraw (baseball)">John McGraw</a>, the Giants\' manager, even went so far as to say that his Giants were already "world champions" since they were the champions of the "only real major league". At the time of the announcement, their new cross-town rivals, the <a href="/wiki/1904_New_York_Highlanders_season" title="1904 New York Highlanders season">New York Highlanders</a> (now the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">New York Yankees</a>), were leading the AL, and the prospect of facing the Highlanders did not please Giants management. Boston won on the last day of the season, and the leagues had previously agreed to hold a World\'s Championship Series in 1904, but it was not binding, and Brush stuck to his original decision. In addition to political reasons, Brush also factually cited the lack of rules under which money would be split, where games would be played, and how they would be operated and staffed.\n</p><p>During the winter of 1904\xe2\x80\x931905, however, feeling the sting of press criticism, Brush had a change of heart and proposed what came to be known as the "Brush Rules", under which the series were played subsequently.  One rule was that player shares would come from a portion of the gate receipts for the first four games only. This was to discourage teams from <a href="/wiki/Match_fixing" title="Match fixing">fixing</a> early games in order to prolong the series and make more money. Receipts for later games would be split among the two clubs and the National Commission, the governing body for the sport, which was able to cover much of its annual operating expense from World Series revenue.  Most importantly, the now-official and compulsory World\'s Series matches were operated strictly by the National Commission itself, not by the participating clubs.\n</p><p>With the new rules in place and the National Commission in control, McGraw\'s <a href="/wiki/1905_New_York_Giants_season" title="1905 New York Giants season">Giants</a> made it to the <a href="/wiki/1905_World_Series" title="1905 World Series">1905 Series</a>, and beat the <a href="/wiki/1905_Philadelphia_Athletics_season" title="1905 Philadelphia Athletics season">Philadelphia Athletics</a> four games to one. Since then the Series has been held every year except 1994, when it was canceled due to a <a href="/wiki/1994%E2%80%9395_Major_League_Baseball_strike" title="1994\xe2\x80\x9395 Major League Baseball strike">players\' strike</a>.\n</p><p>The list of postseason rules evolved over time. In 1925, Brooklyn owner <a href="/wiki/Charles_Ebbets" title="Charles Ebbets">Charles Ebbets</a> persuaded others to adopt as a permanent rule the 2\xe2\x80\x933\xe2\x80\x932 pattern used in <a href="/wiki/1924_World_Series" title="1924 World Series">1924</a>. Prior to 1924, the pattern had been to alternate by game or to make another arrangement convenient to both clubs. The 2\xe2\x80\x933\xe2\x80\x932 pattern has been used ever since save for the <a href="/wiki/1943_World_Series" title="1943 World Series">1943</a> and <a href="/wiki/1945_World_Series" title="1945 World Series">1945 World Series</a>, which followed a 3\xe2\x80\x934 pattern due to World War II travel restrictions; in <a href="/wiki/1944_World_Series" title="1944 World Series">1944</a>, the normal pattern was followed because both teams were based in the same home stadium.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1919_Black_Sox_Scandal">1919 Black Sox Scandal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 1919 Black Sox Scandal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Black_Sox_Scandal" title="Black Sox Scandal">Black Sox Scandal</a></div>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=World_Series&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span>  <small><i>(October 2016)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Gambling and game-fixing had been a problem in professional baseball from the beginning; star pitcher <a href="/wiki/Jim_Devlin" title="Jim Devlin">Jim Devlin</a> was banned for life in 1877, when the National League was just two years old. Baseball\'s gambling problems came to a head in 1919, when eight players of the <a href="/wiki/1919_Chicago_White_Sox_season" title="1919 Chicago White Sox season">Chicago White Sox</a> were alleged to have conspired to throw the <a href="/wiki/1919_World_Series" title="1919 World Series">1919 World Series</a>.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/1917_Chicago_White_Sox_season" title="1917 Chicago White Sox season">Sox</a> had won the Series in <a href="/wiki/1917_World_Series" title="1917 World Series">1917</a> and were heavy favorites to beat the <a href="/wiki/1919_Cincinnati_Reds_season" title="1919 Cincinnati Reds season">Cincinnati Reds</a> in 1919, but first baseman <a href="/wiki/Chick_Gandil" title="Chick Gandil">Chick Gandil</a> had other plans. Gandil, in collaboration with gambler Joseph "Sport" Sullivan, approached his teammates and got six of them to agree to throw the Series: starting pitchers <a href="/wiki/Eddie_Cicotte" title="Eddie Cicotte">Eddie Cicotte</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lefty_Williams" title="Lefty Williams">Lefty Williams</a>, shortstop <a href="/wiki/Swede_Risberg" title="Swede Risberg">Swede Risberg</a>, left fielder <a href="/wiki/Shoeless_Joe_Jackson" title="Shoeless Joe Jackson">Shoeless Joe Jackson</a>, center fielder <a href="/wiki/Happy_Felsch" title="Happy Felsch">Happy Felsch</a>, and utility infielder <a href="/wiki/Fred_McMullin" title="Fred McMullin">Fred McMullin</a>. Third baseman <a href="/wiki/Buck_Weaver" title="Buck Weaver">Buck Weaver</a> knew of the fix but declined to participate, hitting .324 for the series from 11 hits and committing no errors in the field. The Sox, who were promised $100,000 for cooperating, proceeded to lose the Series in eight games, pitching poorly, hitting poorly and making many errors. Though he took the money, Jackson insisted to his death that he played to the best of his ability in the series (he was the best hitter in the series, including having hit the series\' only home run, but had markedly worse numbers in the games the White Sox lost).\n</p><p>During the Series, writer and humorist <a href="/wiki/Ring_Lardner" title="Ring Lardner">Ring Lardner</a> had facetiously called the event the "World\'s Serious". The Series turned out to indeed have serious consequences for the sport. After rumors circulated for nearly a year, the players were suspended in September 1920.\n</p><p>The "<a href="/wiki/Black_Sox" class="mw-redirect" title="Black Sox">Black Sox</a>" were acquitted in a criminal conspiracy trial. However, baseball in the meantime had established the office of <a href="/wiki/Commissioner_of_Baseball" title="Commissioner of Baseball">Commissioner</a> in an effort to protect the game\'s integrity, and the first commissioner, <a href="/wiki/Kenesaw_Mountain_Landis" title="Kenesaw Mountain Landis">Kenesaw Mountain Landis</a>, banned all of the players involved, including Weaver, for life. The White Sox would not win a World Series again until <a href="/wiki/2005_World_Series" title="2005 World Series">2005</a>.\n</p><p>The events of the 1919 Series, segueing into the <a href="/wiki/Live-ball_era" title="Live-ball era">"live ball" era</a>, marked a point in time of change of the fortunes of several teams. The two most prolific World Series winners to date, the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">New York Yankees</a> and the <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Cardinals" title="St. Louis Cardinals">St. Louis Cardinals</a>, did not win their first championship until the 1920s; and three of the teams that were highly successful prior to 1920 (the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Red_Sox" title="Boston Red Sox">Boston Red Sox</a>, Chicago White Sox and the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Cubs" title="Chicago Cubs">Chicago Cubs</a>) went the rest of the 20th century without another World Series win. The Red Sox and White Sox finally won again in 2004 and 2005, respectively.  The Cubs had to wait over a century (until the 2016 season) for their next trophy. They did not appear in the Fall Classic from 1945 until 2016, the longest drought of any MLB club.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="New_York_Yankees_dynasty_.281920.E2.80.931964.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="New_York_Yankees_dynasty_(1920\xe2\x80\x931964)">New York Yankees dynasty (1920\xe2\x80\x931964)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: New York Yankees dynasty (1920\xe2\x80\x931964)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The New York Yankees purchased <a href="/wiki/Babe_Ruth" title="Babe Ruth">Babe Ruth</a> from the Boston Red Sox after the 1919 season, appeared in their first <a href="/wiki/1921_World_Series" title="1921 World Series">World Series</a> two years later in <a href="/wiki/1921_New_York_Yankees_season" title="1921 New York Yankees season">1921</a>, and became frequent participants thereafter.  Over a period of 45 years from 1920 to 1964, the Yankees played in 29 World Series championships, winning 20.  The team\'s dynasty reached its apex between 1947 and 1964, when the Yankees reached the World Series 15 times in eighteen years, helped by an <a href="/wiki/Arnold_Johnson_(industrialist)" title="Arnold Johnson (industrialist)">agreement</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Kansas_City_Athletics" class="mw-redirect" title="Kansas City Athletics">Kansas City Athletics</a> (after that team moved from Philadelphia during 1954\xe2\x80\x931955 offseason) whereby the teams made several deals advantageous to the Yankees (until ended by new Athletics\' owner Charles O. Finley). During that span, the Yankees played in all World Series except <a href="/wiki/1948_World_Series" title="1948 World Series">1948</a>, <a href="/wiki/1954_World_Series" title="1954 World Series">1954</a>, and <a href="/wiki/1959_World_Series" title="1959 World Series">1959</a>, winning ten.  From 1949 to 1953, the Yankees won the World Series five years in a row; from 1936\xe2\x80\x931939 the Yankees won four World Series Championships in a row. There are only two other occasions when a team has won at least three consecutive World Series: 1972 to 1974 by the <a href="/wiki/Oakland_Athletics" title="Oakland Athletics">Oakland Athletics</a>, and 1998 to 2000 by the New York Yankees.\n</p>\n<h4><span id="1947.E2.80.931964:_New_York_City_teams_dominate_World_Series_play"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1947\xe2\x80\x931964:_New_York_City_teams_dominate_World_Series_play">1947\xe2\x80\x931964: New York City teams dominate World Series play</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 1947\xe2\x80\x931964: New York City teams dominate World Series play">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>In an 18-year span from 1947 to 1964, except for 1948 and 1959, the World Series was played in New York City, featuring at least one of the three teams located in New York at the time. The Dodgers and Giants moved to California after the 1957 season, leaving the Yankees as the lone team in the city until the Mets were enfranchised in 1962. During this period, other than 1948, 1954, and 1959, the Yankees represented the American League in the World Series.\n</p><p>In the years 1947, 1949, 1951\xe2\x80\x931953, and 1955\xe2\x80\x931956, both teams in the World Series were from New York, with the Yankees playing against either the Dodgers or Giants.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_World_Series_in_California">The World Series in California</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: The World Series in California">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 1958, the <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Brooklyn_Dodgers" title="History of the Brooklyn Dodgers">Brooklyn Dodgers</a> and <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_New_York_Giants_(NL)" class="mw-redirect" title="History of the New York Giants (NL)">New York Giants</a> took their long-time rivalry to the west coast, <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_relocation_of_1950s%E2%80%931960s#The_exit_of_the_National_League_from_New_York_City" class="mw-redirect" title="Major League Baseball relocation of 1950s\xe2\x80\x931960s">moving</a> to Los Angeles and San Francisco, respectively, bringing Major League Baseball west of St. Louis and Kansas City.\n</p><p>The Dodgers were the first of the two clubs to contest a World Series on the west coast, defeating the <a href="/wiki/1959_Chicago_White_Sox_season" title="1959 Chicago White Sox season">Chicago White Sox</a> in <a href="/wiki/1959_World_Series" title="1959 World Series">1959</a>. The <a href="/wiki/1962_San_Francisco_Giants_season" title="1962 San Francisco Giants season">1962 Giants</a> made the first California World Series appearance of that franchise, losing to the Yankees. The Dodgers made three World Series appearances in the 1960s: a 1963 win over the <a href="/wiki/1963_New_York_Yankees_season" title="1963 New York Yankees season">Yankees</a>, a 1965 win over the <a href="/wiki/1965_Minnesota_Twins_season" title="1965 Minnesota Twins season">Minnesota Twins</a> and a 1966 loss to the <a href="/wiki/1966_Baltimore_Orioles_season" title="1966 Baltimore Orioles season">Baltimore Orioles</a>.\n</p><p>In 1968, the <a href="/wiki/Kansas_City_Athletics" class="mw-redirect" title="Kansas City Athletics">Kansas City Athletics</a> relocated to Oakland and the following year 1969, the <a href="/wiki/National_League" title="National League">National League</a> granted a franchise to San Diego as the <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Padres" title="San Diego Padres">San Diego Padres</a>. The A\'s became a powerful dynasty, winning three consecutive World Series from 1972\xe2\x80\x931974. In <a href="/wiki/1974_World_Series" title="1974 World Series">1974</a>, the A\'s played the Dodgers in the first all-California World Series.  The Padres have two World Series appearances (a 1984 loss to the Detroit Tigers, and a 1998 loss to the New York Yankees).\n</p><p>The Dodgers won two more World Series in the 1980s (1981, 1988). The A\'s again went to three straight world series, from 1988\xe2\x80\x931990, winning once. 1988 and 1989 were all-California series as the A\'s lost to the Dodgers and beat the Giants, respectively. The Giants have been in four World Series\' in the new millennium, losing in 2002 to the Anaheim Angels (<a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Angels_of_Anaheim" class="mw-redirect" title="Los Angeles Angels of Anaheim">Los Angeles Angels of Anaheim</a> from 2005 to 2015), and winning in 2010 (Rangers), 2012 (Tigers), and 2014 (Royals).\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1969:_League_Championship_Series">1969: League Championship Series</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: 1969: League Championship Series">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Prior to 1969, the National League and the American League each crowned its champion (the "pennant winner") based on the best win-loss record at the end of the regular season.\n</p><p>A structured playoff series began in 1969, when both the National and American Leagues were reorganized into two divisions each, East and West. The two division winners within each league played each other in a best-of-five <a href="/wiki/League_Championship_Series" title="League Championship Series">League Championship Series</a> to determine who would advance to the World Series. In 1985, the format changed to best-of-seven.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/National_League_Championship_Series" title="National League Championship Series">National League Championship Series</a> (NLCS) and <a href="/wiki/American_League_Championship_Series" title="American League Championship Series">American League Championship Series</a> (ALCS), since the expansion to best-of-seven, are always played in a 2\xe2\x80\x933\xe2\x80\x932 format: Games 1, 2, 6 and 7 are played in the stadium of the team that has home-field advantage, and Games 3, 4 and 5 are played in the stadium of the team that does not.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1970s">1970s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: 1970s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1971:_World_Series_at_night">1971: World Series at night</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: 1971: World Series at night">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>MLB night games started being held in 1935 by the <a href="/wiki/1935_Cincinnati_Reds_season" title="1935 Cincinnati Reds season">Cincinnati Reds</a>, but the World Series remained a strictly daytime event for years thereafter. In the final game of the <a href="/wiki/1949_World_Series" title="1949 World Series">1949 World Series</a>, a Series game was finished under lights for the first time. The first scheduled night World Series game was Game 4 of the <a href="/wiki/1971_World_Series" title="1971 World Series">1971 World Series</a> at <a href="/wiki/Three_Rivers_Stadium" title="Three Rivers Stadium">Three Rivers Stadium</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>  Afterward, World Series games were frequently scheduled at night, when television audiences were larger. Game 6 of the <a href="/wiki/1987_World_Series" title="1987 World Series">1987 World Series</a> was the last World Series game played in the daytime,<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> indoors at the <a href="/wiki/Metrodome" class="mw-redirect" title="Metrodome">Metrodome</a> in Minnesota. (The last World Series played outdoors during the day was the final game of the <a href="/wiki/1984_World_Series" title="1984 World Series">1984 series</a> in Detroit\'s <a href="/wiki/Tiger_Stadium_(Detroit)" title="Tiger Stadium (Detroit)">Tiger Stadium</a>.)\n</p>\n<h4><span id="1972.E2.80.931978:_Threepeat.2C_repeats.2C_and_Fisk.27s_home_run"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1972\xe2\x80\x931978:_Threepeat,_repeats,_and_Fisk\'s_home_run">1972\xe2\x80\x931978: Threepeat, repeats, and Fisk\'s home run</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: 1972\xe2\x80\x931978: Threepeat, repeats, and Fisk&#039;s home run">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>During this seven-year period, only three teams won the World Series: the <a href="/wiki/Oakland_Athletics" title="Oakland Athletics">Oakland Athletics</a> from 1972 to 1974, <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati_Reds" title="Cincinnati Reds">Cincinnati Reds</a> in 1975 and 1976, and <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">New York Yankees</a> in 1977 and 1978. This is the only time in World Series history in which three teams have won consecutive series in succession. This period was book-ended by World Championships for the <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Pirates" title="Pittsburgh Pirates">Pittsburgh Pirates</a>, in 1971 and 1979.\n</p><p>However, the <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Orioles" title="Baltimore Orioles">Baltimore Orioles</a> made three consecutive World Series appearances: 1969 (losing to the "amazing" eight-year-old franchise <a href="/wiki/New_York_Mets" title="New York Mets">New York Mets</a>), 1970 (beating the Reds in their first World Series appearance of the decade), and 1971 (losing to the Pittsburgh Pirates, as well their 1979 appearance, when they again lost to the Pirates), and the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Dodgers" title="Los Angeles Dodgers">Los Angeles Dodgers</a>\' back-to-back World Series appearances in 1977 and 1978 (both losses to the New York Yankees), as well in 1974 losing against the cross-state rival Oakland Athletics.\n</p><p>Game 6 of the <a href="/wiki/1975_World_Series" title="1975 World Series">1975 World Series</a> is regarded by most as one of the greatest World Series games ever played. It found the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Red_Sox" title="Boston Red Sox">Boston Red Sox</a> winning in the 12th inning in <a href="/wiki/Fenway_Park" title="Fenway Park">Fenway Park</a>, defeating the Cincinnati Reds to force a seventh and deciding game. The game is best remembered for its exciting lead changes, nail-biting turns of events, and a game-winning <a href="/wiki/Walk-off_home_run" title="Walk-off home run">walk-off home run</a> by <a href="/wiki/Carlton_Fisk" title="Carlton Fisk">Carlton Fisk</a>, resulting in a 7\xe2\x80\x936 Red Sox victory.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1976:_The_designated_hitter_comes_to_the_World_Series">1976: The designated hitter comes to the World Series</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: 1976: The designated hitter comes to the World Series">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The National and American Leagues operated under essentially identical rules until 1973, when the American League adopted the <a href="/wiki/Designated_hitter" title="Designated hitter">designated hitter</a> (DH) rule, allowing its teams to use another hitter to bat in place of the (usually) weak-hitting pitcher.  The National League did not adopt the DH rule.  This presented a problem for the World Series, whose two contestants would now be playing their regular-season games under different rules. From 1973 to 1975, the World Series did not include a DH. Starting in 1976, the World Series allowed for the use of a DH in even-numbered years only. (The <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati_Reds" title="Cincinnati Reds">Cincinnati Reds</a> swept the 1976 Series in four games, using the same nine-man lineup in each contest. <a href="/wiki/Dan_Driessen" title="Dan Driessen">Dan Driessen</a> was the Reds\' DH during the series, thereby becoming the National League\'s first designated hitter.) Finally, in 1986, baseball adopted the current rule in which the DH is used for World Series games played in the AL champion\'s park but not the NL champion\'s. Thus, the DH rule\'s use or non-use can affect the performance of the home team.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1980s">1980s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: 1980s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1984:_Anderson_becomes_first_to_win_in_both_leagues">1984: Anderson becomes first to win in both leagues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: 1984: Anderson becomes first to win in both leagues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/1984_Detroit_Tigers_season" title="1984 Detroit Tigers season">1984 Detroit Tigers</a> gained distinction as just the third team in major league history (after the 1927 New York Yankees and 1955 Brooklyn Dodgers) to lead a season wire-to-wire, from opening day through their World Series victory.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> In the process, Tigers skipper <a href="/wiki/Sparky_Anderson" title="Sparky Anderson">Sparky Anderson</a> became the first manager to win a World Series title in both leagues, having previously won in 1975 and 1976 with the <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati_Reds" title="Cincinnati Reds">Cincinnati Reds</a>.\n</p>\n<h4><span id="1988:_Kirk_Gibson.27s_home_run"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1988:_Kirk_Gibson\'s_home_run">1988: Kirk Gibson\'s home run</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: 1988: Kirk Gibson&#039;s home run">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/1988_World_Series" title="1988 World Series">1988 World Series</a> is remembered for the iconic home run by the Los Angeles Dodgers\' <a href="/wiki/Kirk_Gibson" title="Kirk Gibson">Kirk Gibson</a> with two outs in the bottom of the ninth inning of Game 1.  The Dodgers were huge underdogs against the 104-win Oakland Athletics, who had swept the Boston Red Sox in the ALCS.  Baseball\'s top relief pitcher, <a href="/wiki/Dennis_Eckersley" title="Dennis Eckersley">Dennis Eckersley</a>, closed out all four games in the ALCS, and he appeared ready to do the same in Game 1 against a Dodgers team trailing 4\xe2\x80\x933 in the ninth.  After getting the first two outs, Eckersley walked <a href="/wiki/Mike_Davis_(baseball)" title="Mike Davis (baseball)">Mike Davis</a> of the Dodgers, who were playing without Gibson, their best position player and the NL MVP.  Gibson had injured himself in the NLCS and was expected to miss the entire World Series.  Yet, despite not being able to walk without a noticeable limp, Gibson surprised all in attendance at Dodger Stadium (and all watching on TV) by pinch-hitting.  After two quick strikes and then working the count full, Gibson hit a home run to right, inspiring iconic pronouncements by two legendary broadcasters calling the game, <a href="/wiki/Vin_Scully" title="Vin Scully">Vin Scully</a> (on TV) and <a href="/wiki/Jack_Buck" title="Jack Buck">Jack Buck</a> (on radio).  On NBC, as Gibson limped around the bases, Scully famously exclaimed, "The impossible has happened!" and on radio, Buck equally famously exclaimed, "I don\'t believe what I just saw!" Gibson\'s home run set the tone for the series, as the Dodgers went on to beat the A\'s 4 games to 1.  The severity of Gibson\'s injury prevented him from playing in any of the remaining games.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1989:_Earthquake">1989: Earthquake</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: 1989: Earthquake">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=World_Series&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span>  <small><i>(October 2016)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>When the <a href="/wiki/1989_World_Series" title="1989 World Series">1989 World Series</a> began, it was notable chiefly for being the first ever World Series matchup between the two <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Bay_Area" title="San Francisco Bay Area">San Francisco Bay Area</a> teams, the <a href="/wiki/1989_San_Francisco_Giants_season" title="1989 San Francisco Giants season">San Francisco Giants</a> and <a href="/wiki/1989_Oakland_Athletics_season" title="1989 Oakland Athletics season">Oakland Athletics</a>. Oakland won the first two games at home, and the two teams crossed the bridge to San Francisco to play Game 3 on Tuesday, October 17. <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_on_ABC" title="Major League Baseball on ABC">ABC</a>\'s broadcast of Game 3 began at 5&#160;pm local time, approximately 30 minutes before the first pitch was scheduled. At 5:04, while broadcasters <a href="/wiki/Al_Michaels" title="Al Michaels">Al Michaels</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tim_McCarver" title="Tim McCarver">Tim McCarver</a> were narrating highlights and the teams were warming up, the <a href="/wiki/Loma_Prieta_earthquake" class="mw-redirect" title="Loma Prieta earthquake">Loma Prieta earthquake</a> occurred (having a surface-wave magnitude of 7.1 with an epicenter ten miles (16&#160;km) northeast of Santa Cruz, California). The earthquake caused substantial property and economic damage in the Bay Area and killed 63 people. Television viewers saw the video signal deteriorate and heard Michaels say "I\'ll tell you what, we\'re having an earth--" before the feed from <a href="/wiki/Candlestick_Park" title="Candlestick Park">Candlestick Park</a> was lost. Fans filing into the stadium saw Candlestick sway visibly during the quake. Television coverage later resumed, using backup generators, with Michaels becoming a news reporter on the unfolding disaster. Approximately 30 minutes after the earthquake, Commissioner <a href="/wiki/Fay_Vincent" title="Fay Vincent">Fay Vincent</a> ordered the game to be postponed. Fans, workers, and the teams evacuated a blacked out (although still sunlit) Candlestick. Game 3 was finally played on October 27, and Oakland won that day and the next to complete a four-game sweep.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1990s">1990s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: 1990s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<h4><span id="1992.E2.80.931993:_The_World_Series_enters_Canada"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1992\xe2\x80\x931993:_The_World_Series_enters_Canada">1992\xe2\x80\x931993: The World Series enters Canada</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: 1992\xe2\x80\x931993: The World Series enters Canada">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>World Series games were contested outside of the United States for the first time in <a href="/wiki/1992_World_Series" title="1992 World Series">1992</a>, with the <a href="/wiki/1992_Toronto_Blue_Jays_season" title="1992 Toronto Blue Jays season">Toronto Blue Jays</a> defeating the <a href="/wiki/1992_Atlanta_Braves_season" title="1992 Atlanta Braves season">Atlanta Braves</a> in six games. The World Series returned to Canada in <a href="/wiki/1993_World_Series" title="1993 World Series">1993</a>, with the <a href="/wiki/1993_Toronto_Blue_Jays" class="mw-redirect" title="1993 Toronto Blue Jays">Blue Jays</a> victorious again, this time against the <a href="/wiki/1993_Philadelphia_Phillies_season" title="1993 Philadelphia Phillies season">Philadelphia Phillies</a> in six games. No other Series has featured a team from outside of the United States. Toronto is the only expansion team to win successive World Series titles. The 1993 World Series was also notable for being only the second championship concluded by a home run and the first concluded by a come-from-behind homer, after <a href="/wiki/Joe_Carter" title="Joe Carter">Joe Carter</a>\'s three-run shot in the bottom of the ninth inning sealed an 8\xe2\x80\x936 Toronto win in Game 6. The first Series to end with a homer was the <a href="/wiki/1960_World_Series" title="1960 World Series">1960 World Series</a>, when <a href="/wiki/Bill_Mazeroski" title="Bill Mazeroski">Bill Mazeroski</a> hit a ninth-inning solo shot in Game 7 to win the championship for the <a href="/wiki/1960_Pittsburgh_Pirates_season" title="1960 Pittsburgh Pirates season">Pittsburgh Pirates</a>.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1994:_League_Division_Series">1994: League Division Series</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: 1994: League Division Series">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>In 1994, each league was restructured into three divisions, with the three division winners and the newly introduced wild card winner advancing to a best-of-five playoff round (the "<a href="/wiki/Division_Series" title="Division Series">division series</a>"), the <a href="/wiki/National_League_Division_Series" title="National League Division Series">National League Division Series</a> (NLDS) and <a href="/wiki/American_League_Division_Series" title="American League Division Series">American League Division Series</a> (ALDS).  The team with the best league record is matched against the wild card team, unless they are in the same division, in which case, the team with the second-best record plays against the wild card winner. The remaining two division winners are pitted against each other. The winners of the series in the first round advance to the best-of-seven NLCS and ALCS. Due to a players\' strike, however, the NLDS and ALDS were not played until 1995.  Beginning in 1998, home field advantage was given to the team with the better regular season record, with the exception that the Wild Card team cannot get home-field advantage.\n</p>\n<h4><span id="1994.E2.80.931995_strike"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1994\xe2\x80\x931995_strike">1994\xe2\x80\x931995 strike</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: 1994\xe2\x80\x931995 strike">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/1994%E2%80%9395_Major_League_Baseball_strike" title="1994\xe2\x80\x9395 Major League Baseball strike">1994\xe2\x80\x9395 Major League Baseball strike</a></div>\n<p>After the boycott of <a href="/wiki/1904_World_Series" title="1904 World Series">1904</a>, the World Series was played every year until 1994 despite the First World War, the <a href="/wiki/1918_flu_pandemic" class="mw-redirect" title="1918 flu pandemic">global influenza pandemic of 1918\xe2\x80\x931919</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a> of the 1930s, America\'s involvement in the Second World War, and even an <a href="/wiki/1989_Loma_Prieta_earthquake" title="1989 Loma Prieta earthquake">earthquake</a> in the host cities of the <a href="/wiki/1989_World_Series" title="1989 World Series">1989 World Series</a>. A breakdown in collective bargaining led to a strike in August 1994 and the eventual cancellation of the rest of the season, including the playoffs.\n</p><p>As the labor talks began, baseball franchise owners demanded a <a href="/wiki/Salary_cap" title="Salary cap">salary cap</a> in order to limit payrolls, the elimination of <a href="/wiki/Salary_arbitration" class="mw-redirect" title="Salary arbitration">salary arbitration</a>, and the right to retain free agent players by matching a competitor\'s best offer.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_Players_Association" title="Major League Baseball Players Association">Major League Baseball Players Association</a> (MLBPA) refused to agree to limit payrolls, noting that the responsibility for high payrolls lay with those owners who were voluntarily offering contracts. One difficulty in reaching a settlement was the absence of a <a href="/wiki/Baseball_Commissioner" class="mw-redirect" title="Baseball Commissioner">commissioner</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> When <a href="/wiki/Fay_Vincent" title="Fay Vincent">Fay Vincent</a> was forced to resign in 1992, owners did not replace him, electing instead to make <a href="/wiki/Milwaukee_Brewers" title="Milwaukee Brewers">Milwaukee Brewers</a> owner <a href="/wiki/Bud_Selig" title="Bud Selig">Bud Selig</a> acting commissioner. Thus, baseball headed into the <a href="/wiki/1994%E2%80%9395_Major_League_Baseball_strike" title="1994\xe2\x80\x9395 Major League Baseball strike">1994 work stoppage</a> without a full-time commissioner for the first time since the office was founded in 1920.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>The previous collective bargaining agreement expired on December 31, 1993, and baseball began the 1994 season without a new agreement. Owners and players negotiated as the season progressed, but owners refused to give up the idea of a salary cap and players refused to accept one. On August 12, 1994, the players went on strike. After a month passed with no progress in the labor talks, Selig canceled the rest of the 1994 season and the postseason on September 14. The <a href="/wiki/1994_World_Series" title="1994 World Series">World Series</a> was not played for the first time in 90 years. The <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Expos" title="Montreal Expos">Montreal Expos</a>, now the <b><a href="/wiki/Washington_Nationals" title="Washington Nationals">Washington Nationals</a></b>, were the best team in baseball at the time of the stoppage, with a record of 74\xe2\x80\x9340 (since their founding in 1969, the Expos/Nationals have never played in a World Series.)\n</p><p>The labor dispute lasted into the spring of 1995, with owners beginning <a href="/wiki/Spring_training" title="Spring training">spring training</a> with replacement players. However, the MLBPA returned to work on April 2, 1995 after a federal judge, future <a href="/wiki/U.S._Supreme_Court" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Supreme Court">U.S. Supreme Court</a> justice <a href="/wiki/Sonia_Sotomayor" title="Sonia Sotomayor">Sonia Sotomayor</a>, ruled that the owners had engaged in unfair labor practices.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The season started on April 25 and the <a href="/wiki/1995_World_Series" title="1995 World Series">1995 World Series</a> was played as scheduled, with <a href="/wiki/1995_Atlanta_Braves_season" title="1995 Atlanta Braves season">Atlanta</a> beating <a href="/wiki/1995_Cleveland_Indians_season" title="1995 Cleveland Indians season">Cleveland</a> four games to two.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2000s">2000s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: 2000s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/2001_World_Series" title="2001 World Series">2001 World Series</a> was the first World Series to end in November, due to the week-long delay in the regular season after the <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">September 11 attacks</a>. Game 4  had begun on Oct. 31 but went into extra innings and ended early on the morning of Nov. 1, the first time the Series had been played in November. Yankee shortstop <a href="/wiki/Derek_Jeter" title="Derek Jeter">Derek Jeter</a> won the game with a 12th inning <a href="/wiki/Walk-off_home_run" title="Walk-off home run">walk-off home run</a> and was dubbed "Mr. November" by elements of the media \xe2\x80\x93 echoing the media\'s designation of <a href="/wiki/Reggie_Jackson" title="Reggie Jackson">Reggie Jackson</a> as "Mr. October" for his slugging achievements during the <a href="/wiki/1977_World_Series" title="1977 World Series">1977 World Series</a>.\n</p><p>With the <a href="/wiki/2006_World_Series" title="2006 World Series">2006 World Series</a> victory by the <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Cardinals" title="St. Louis Cardinals">St. Louis Cardinals</a>, Tony La Russa became the second manager to a win a World Series in both the American and National Leagues.\n</p>\n<h4><span id="All-Star_Game_and_home-field_advantage_.282003.E2.80.932016.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="All-Star_Game_and_home-field_advantage_(2003\xe2\x80\x932016)">All-Star Game and home-field advantage (2003\xe2\x80\x932016)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: All-Star Game and home-field advantage (2003\xe2\x80\x932016)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Prior to 2003, <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_postseason#Home-field_advantage" title="Major League Baseball postseason">home-field advantage</a> in the World Series alternated from year to year between the NL and AL. After the <a href="/wiki/2002_Major_League_Baseball_All-Star_Game" title="2002 Major League Baseball All-Star Game">2002 Major League Baseball All-Star Game</a> ended in a tie, MLB decided to award home-field advantage in the World Series to the winner of the <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_All-Star_Game" title="Major League Baseball All-Star Game">All-Star Game</a>. Originally implemented as a two-year trial from 2003 to 2004, the practice was extended.\n</p><p>The American League had won every All-Star Game since this change until 2010 and thus enjoyed home-field advantage from 2002, when it also had home-field advantage based on the alternating schedule, through 2009. From 2003 to 2010, the AL and NL had each won the World Series four times, but none of them had gone the full seven games. Since then, the <a href="/wiki/2011_World_Series" title="2011 World Series">2011</a>, <a href="/wiki/2014_World_Series" title="2014 World Series">2014</a>, <a href="/wiki/2016_World_Series" title="2016 World Series">2016</a>, and <a href="/wiki/2017_World_Series" title="2017 World Series">2017 World Series</a> have gone the full seven games.\n</p><p>This rule was subject to debate, with various writers feeling that home-field advantage should be decided based on the regular season records of the participants, not on an exhibition game played several months earlier.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Some writers especially questioned the integrity of this rule after the <a href="/wiki/2014_Major_League_Baseball_All-Star_Game" title="2014 Major League Baseball All-Star Game">2014 All-Star Game</a>, when <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Cardinals" title="St. Louis Cardinals">St. Louis Cardinals</a> pitcher <a href="/wiki/Adam_Wainwright" title="Adam Wainwright">Adam Wainwright</a> suggested that he intentionally gave <a href="/wiki/Derek_Jeter" title="Derek Jeter">Derek Jeter</a> some easy pitches to hit in the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">New York Yankees</a>\' shortstop\'s final All-Star appearance before he retired at the end of that season.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As <a href="/wiki/Bob_Ryan" title="Bob Ryan">Bob Ryan</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Boston_Globe" title="The Boston Globe">The Boston Globe</a></i> wrote in July 2015 about the rule:\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303468">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>"So now we have a game that\'s not real baseball determining which league hosts Games 1, 2, 6, and 7 in the World Series. It\'s not a game if pitchers throw one inning. It\'s not a game if managers try to get everyone on a bloated roster into the game. It\'s not a game if every franchise, no matter how wretched, has to put a player on the team ... If the game is going to count, tell the managers to channel their inner <a href="/wiki/Connie_Mack" title="Connie Mack">Connie Mack</a> and go for it."<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>\n</p></blockquote>\n<p>However, within the last seven seasons, home-field advantage, in terms of deciding World Series games, has not necessarily worked for teams of said games. Since 2014, the home team has not won the deciding game of a World Series.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2010s">2010s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: 2010s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Giants" title="San Francisco Giants">San Francisco Giants</a> won the World Series in <a href="/wiki/2010_World_Series" title="2010 World Series">2010</a>, <a href="/wiki/2012_World_Series" title="2012 World Series">2012</a>, and <a href="/wiki/2014_World_Series" title="2014 World Series">2014</a> while failing to qualify to play in the postseason in the intervening seasons.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Texas_Rangers_(baseball)" title="Texas Rangers (baseball)">Texas Rangers</a> were twice only one strike away from winning their first World Series title in <a href="/wiki/2011_World_Series" title="2011 World Series">2011</a>, but the <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Cardinals" title="St. Louis Cardinals">St. Louis Cardinals</a>\' <a href="/wiki/David_Freese" title="David Freese">David Freese</a>, the eventual Series MVP, drove in both the tying and winning runs late in Game 6 to force a Game 7.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Kansas_City_Royals" title="Kansas City Royals">Kansas City Royals</a> reached the World Series in 2014, which was their first appearance in the postseason since winning the series in 1985. At the time, it was the longest postseason drought in baseball. They lost in seven games to the Giants. The following season, the Royals finished with the American League\'s best record, and won a second consecutive American League pennant. They defeated the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Mets" title="New York Mets">New York Mets</a> in the World Series 4\xe2\x80\x931, capturing their first title in 30 years. The 2015 contest was the first time that two expansion clubs met for the Fall Classic.\n</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/2016_World_Series" title="2016 World Series">2016</a>, the Chicago Cubs ended their <a href="/wiki/Curse_of_the_Billy_Goat" title="Curse of the Billy Goat">108-year long drought without a World Series title</a> by defeating the <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Indians" title="Cleveland Indians">Cleveland Indians</a>, rallying from a 3\xe2\x80\x931 Series deficit in the process. That extended Cleveland\'s <a href="/wiki/List_of_Major_League_Baseball_franchise_postseason_droughts" title="List of Major League Baseball franchise postseason droughts">\nWorld Series title drought</a> to 68 years and counting \xe2\x80\x93 the Indians last won the Series in  <a href="/wiki/1948_World_Series" title="1948 World Series">1948</a> \xe2\x80\x93 now the longest title drought in the majors.\n</p><p>Beginning in 2017, home field advantage in the World Series is awarded to the league champion team with the better regular season win-loss record.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> If both league champions have the same record, the second tie-breaker would be head-to-head record, and if that does not resolve it, the third tie-breaker would be best divisional record.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Houston_Astros" title="Houston Astros">Houston Astros</a> won the 2017 World Series in 7 games against the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Dodgers" title="Los Angeles Dodgers">Los Angeles Dodgers</a> on November 1, 2017, winning their first World Series since their creation in 1962.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_World_Series_appearances_by_franchise">Modern World Series appearances by franchise</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Modern World Series appearances by franchise">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_World_Series_champions" title="List of World Series champions">List of World Series champions</a></div>\n<h3><span id="World_Series_record_by_team_or_franchise.2C_1903.E2.80.932017"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="World_Series_record_by_team_or_franchise,_1903\xe2\x80\x932017">World Series record by team or franchise, 1903\xe2\x80\x932017</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: World Series record by team or franchise, 1903\xe2\x80\x932017">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div>\n\n&#32;\n<table class="multicol" role="presentation" style="border-collapse: collapse; padding: 0;
