/><small>[previously Devil Rays]</small>\n</td>\n<td>0\n</td>\n<td>1\n</td>\n<td><span data-sort-value="0&#160;!">\xe2\x80\x94</span>\n</td>\n<td>2008\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="background:#acf;"><a href="/wiki/Colorado_Rockies" title="Colorado Rockies">Colorado Rockies</a> (NL, 1993) *\n</td>\n<td>0\n</td>\n<td>1\n</td>\n<td><span data-sort-value="0&#160;!">\xe2\x80\x94</span>\n</td>\n<td>2007\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="background:#fbd;"><a href="/wiki/Seattle_Mariners" title="Seattle Mariners">Seattle Mariners</a> (AL, 1977) *\n</td>\n<td>0\n</td>\n<td>0\n</td>\n<td><span data-sort-value="0&#160;!">\xe2\x80\x94</span>\n</td>\n<td><span data-sort-value="0&#160;!">\xe2\x80\x94</span>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="background:#acf;"><a href="/wiki/Washington_Nationals" title="Washington Nationals">Washington Nationals</a> (NL, 1969) *<br /><small>[previously Montreal Expos]</small>\n</td>\n<td>0\n</td>\n<td>0\n</td>\n<td><span data-sort-value="0&#160;!">\xe2\x80\x94</span>\n</td>\n<td><span data-sort-value="0&#160;!">\xe2\x80\x94</span>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>&#32;\n</p>\n</td>\n<td style="text-align: left; vertical-align: top;">\n<table class="wikitable" style="margin-left:1em; text-align:center;">\n\n<tbody><tr style="text-align:center;">\n<td style="background:#e3e3e3;"><b>Key to table</b>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>AL = <a href="/wiki/American_League" title="American League">American League</a> <br /> NL = <a href="/wiki/National_League" title="National League">National League</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>* Joined the AL or NL <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball#Expanding_west,_south_and_north" title="Major League Baseball">after 1960</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#f6f6fe;">\n<td>\xe2\x80\xa0 Totals include a team\'s record<br /> with another nickname or in a previous city<br /><small>[bracketed in small type below its current name].<br /> <i>For further details, see individual team articles or <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball#Current_teams" title="Major League Baseball">Major League franchises</a>.</i>\n</small></td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><i>See also:</i> <a href="/wiki/List_of_World_Series_champions" title="List of World Series champions">List of World Series champions</a><br /><small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://mlb.mlb.com/mlb/history/postseason/mlb_ws.jsp?feature=club_champs">MLB.com</a></small>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<p>&#32;\n</p>\n</td></tr></tbody></table></div>\n<dl><dt>Notes</dt></dl>\n<p><a href="/wiki/American_League" title="American League">American League</a> (AL) teams have won 65 of the 113 World Series played (57.5%). The <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">New York Yankees</a> have won 27 titles, accounting for 23.9% of all series played and 41.5% of the wins by American League teams. The <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Cardinals" title="St. Louis Cardinals">St. Louis Cardinals</a> have won 11 World Series, accounting for 9.7% of all series played and 23% of the 48 National League victories.\n</p><p>When the first modern World Series was played in 1903, there were eight teams in each league. These 16 franchises, all of which are still in existence, have each won at least two World Series titles.\n</p><p>The number of teams was unchanged until 1961, with fourteen <a href="/wiki/Expansion_team#Major_League_Baseball" title="Expansion team">expansion teams</a> joining MLB since then. Twelve have played in a World Series (the <a href="/wiki/Seattle_Mariners" title="Seattle Mariners">Mariners</a> and <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Expos" title="Montreal Expos">Expos</a>/<a href="/wiki/Washington_Nationals" title="Washington Nationals">Nationals</a> being the two exceptions). The expansion teams have won ten of the 22 Series (45%) in which they have played, which is 9% of all 113 series played since 1903. In 2015, the first World Series featuring only expansion teams was played between the Kansas City Royals and New York Mets.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Team_patterns_in_the_World_Series">Team patterns in the World Series</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Team patterns in the World Series">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>This information is up to date through the present time:\n</p>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=World_Series&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span>  <small><i>(October 2016)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Streaks_and_droughts">Streaks and droughts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Streaks and droughts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Major_League_Baseball_franchise_postseason_streaks" title="List of Major League Baseball franchise postseason streaks">List of Major League Baseball franchise postseason streaks</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Major_League_Baseball_franchise_postseason_droughts" title="List of Major League Baseball franchise postseason droughts">List of Major League Baseball franchise postseason droughts</a></div>\n<ol><li>Since their first championship in <a href="/wiki/1923_New_York_Yankees_season" title="1923 New York Yankees season">1923</a>, the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">New York Yankees</a> have won two or more World Series titles in every decade except the 1980s, when they won none, and now the 2010s, where only one chance remains for them to win one this decade. Additionally, they have won at least one American League pennant in every decade since the 1920s.  (They have yet to win a pennant or Series in the 2010s.) The Yankees are the only team in either League to win more than three series in a row, winning in four consecutive seasons from 1936 to 1939, and a still MLB record five consecutive seasons from 1949 to 1953.  The Yankees also won three consecutive World Series from 1998 to 2000.  The only team other than the Yankees to win three consecutive World Series is the <a href="/wiki/Oakland_Athletics" title="Oakland Athletics">Oakland Athletics</a>, who won the Series in 1972, 1973, and 1974.</li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/New_York_Giants_(NL)" class="mw-redirect" title="New York Giants (NL)">New York Giants</a>\' four World Series appearances from 1921 to 1924 are the most consecutive appearances for any National League franchise.  The Yankees are the only American League franchise to appear in four or more consecutive World Series.</li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/1907_World_Series" title="1907 World Series">1907</a>\xe2\x80\x93<a href="/wiki/1908_World_Series" title="1908 World Series">1908</a> Cubs, <a href="/wiki/1921_World_Series" title="1921 World Series">1921</a>\xe2\x80\x93<a href="/wiki/1922_World_Series" title="1922 World Series">1922</a> Giants and the <a href="/wiki/1975_World_Series" title="1975 World Series">1975</a>\xe2\x80\x93<a href="/wiki/1976_World_Series" title="1976 World Series">1976</a> Reds are the only National League teams to win back-to-back World Series.  No National League team has ever won three consecutive World Series.</li>\n<li>The 1907\xe2\x80\x931909 <a href="/wiki/Detroit_Tigers" title="Detroit Tigers">Detroit Tigers</a> and the 1911\xe2\x80\x931913 <a href="/wiki/New_York_Giants_(NL)" class="mw-redirect" title="New York Giants (NL)">New York Giants</a> are the only teams to lose three consecutive World Series.</li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Cubs" title="Chicago Cubs">Chicago Cubs</a> hold the record for the longest World Series championship drought of all time, with no titles between <a href="/wiki/1908_World_Series" title="1908 World Series">1908</a> and <a href="/wiki/2016_World_Series" title="2016 World Series">2016</a> (108 years). They also hold the longest ever pennant drought of all time, which stretched from 1945 to 2016. Their pennant drought ended with a 4\xe2\x80\x932 series victory over the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Dodgers" title="Los Angeles Dodgers">Los Angeles Dodgers</a> in the 2016 NLCS.  With the Cubs\' subsequent victory in the 2016 World Series, the longest active World Series championship drought belongs coincidentally to their opponents in that series, the <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Indians" title="Cleveland Indians">Cleveland Indians</a>, who have not won a World Series since 1948.  The Indians\' drought is the second longest active championship drought among all four major professional sports leagues in North America (MLB, NBA, NFL, and NHL); only the NFL\'s <a href="/wiki/Arizona_Cardinals" title="Arizona Cardinals">Arizona Cardinals</a>, who last won a league championship in 1947, when the team still operated as the Chicago Cardinals, have a longer active championship drought.  The team with the longest active pennant drought among AL teams that have played in a World Series at least once is the <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Orioles" title="Baltimore Orioles">Baltimore Orioles</a>, who have not reached a World Series since winning their last title in 1983. The team with the longest active pennant drought among NL teams that have played in a World Series at least once is the <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Pirates" title="Pittsburgh Pirates">Pittsburgh Pirates</a>, who have not reached a World Series since winning their last title in 1979.  This also means that the Pirates hold the second longest active World Series title drought among all teams that have at least one Series and longest championship drought among NL teams that have won a Series.</li>\n<li>Twenty-three of the 28 teams to play in the World Series have won it at least once. The only exceptions are: <a href="/wiki/Milwaukee_Brewers" title="Milwaukee Brewers">Milwaukee Brewers</a> (formerly Seattle Pilots, 1969), <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Padres" title="San Diego Padres">San Diego Padres</a> (1969), <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Rockies" title="Colorado Rockies">Colorado Rockies</a> (1993), <a href="/wiki/Tampa_Bay_Rays" title="Tampa Bay Rays">Tampa Bay Rays</a> (formerly Devil Rays, 1998), and <a href="/wiki/Texas_Rangers_(baseball)" title="Texas Rangers (baseball)">Texas Rangers</a> (formerly Washington Senators, 1961).  The Padres and Rangers have both lost two World Series; the remaining teams have all lost their only Series appearance.  As of the present, all teams with three or more World Series appearances have won the World Series at least once.</li>\n<li>Two teams have never played in the World Series: the National League\'s <a href="/wiki/Washington_Nationals" title="Washington Nationals">Washington Nationals</a> (formerly Montreal Expos, established in 1969), and the American League\'s <a href="/wiki/Seattle_Mariners" title="Seattle Mariners">Seattle Mariners</a> (established in 1977). Both franchises have participated in post-season play and competed in a League Championship Series at least once, but neither team has any League Championship Series victories.</li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/Boston_Red_Sox" title="Boston Red Sox">Red Sox</a> have the most World Series titles before their first World Series loss, winning the championship in their first five appearances\xe2\x80\x94<a href="/wiki/1903_World_Series" title="1903 World Series">1903</a>, <a href="/wiki/1912_World_Series" title="1912 World Series">1912</a>, <a href="/wiki/1915_World_Series" title="1915 World Series">1915</a>, <a href="/wiki/1916_World_Series" title="1916 World Series">1916</a>, and <a href="/wiki/1918_World_Series" title="1918 World Series">1918</a>\xe2\x80\x94before losing in the next series they played, in <a href="/wiki/1946_World_Series" title="1946 World Series">1946</a>. The only other teams who have more than one Series victory before their first Series loss are the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_White_Sox" title="Chicago White Sox">Chicago White Sox</a> (in <a href="/wiki/1906_World_Series" title="1906 World Series">1906</a> and <a href="/wiki/1917_World_Series" title="1917 World Series">1917</a>), the <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Indians" title="Cleveland Indians">Cleveland Indians</a> (in <a href="/wiki/1920_World_Series" title="1920 World Series">1920</a> and <a href="/wiki/1948_World_Series" title="1948 World Series">1948</a>), the <a href="/wiki/Toronto_Blue_Jays" title="Toronto Blue Jays">Toronto Blue Jays</a> (in <a href="/wiki/1992_World_Series" title="1992 World Series">1992</a> and <a href="/wiki/1993_World_Series" title="1993 World Series">1993</a>), and the <a href="/wiki/Miami_Marlins" title="Miami Marlins">Miami Marlins</a> (in <a href="/wiki/1997_World_Series" title="1997 World Series">1997</a> and <a href="/wiki/2003_World_Series" title="2003 World Series">2003</a> as the Florida Marlins). The Blue Jays and the Marlins have never lost a World Series.</li>\n<li>The American League\'s Toronto Blue Jays (1992 and 1993) and National League\'s Miami Marlins (1997 and 2003 as the Florida Marlins) hold the record for most appearances in a Series without ever losing a Series.  Two other franchises have won their lone appearance: the National League\'s Arizona Diamondbacks (2001) and American League\'s Los Angeles Angels (2002 as the Anaheim Angels).</li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Pirates" title="Pittsburgh Pirates">Pirates</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati_Reds" title="Cincinnati Reds">Reds</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boston_Red_Sox" title="Boston Red Sox">Red Sox</a>, and <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Giants" title="San Francisco Giants">Giants</a> are tied with the longest active streak of World Series victories (three) since the last time they lost a series.  Since losing the <a href="/wiki/1927_World_Series" title="1927 World Series">1927</a> series to the Yankees, the Pirates have emerged victorious in the next three series in which they have played (<a href="/wiki/1960_World_Series" title="1960 World Series">1960</a>, <a href="/wiki/1971_World_Series" title="1971 World Series">1971</a>, and <a href="/wiki/1979_World_Series" title="1979 World Series">1979</a>).  The Reds last series loss prior to their current active streak of three titles (<a href="/wiki/1975_World_Series" title="1975 World Series">1975</a>, <a href="/wiki/1976_World_Series" title="1976 World Series">1976</a>, and <a href="/wiki/1990_World_Series" title="1990 World Series">1990</a>) was in <a href="/wiki/1972_World_Series" title="1972 World Series">1972</a>.  The <a href="/wiki/Boston_Red_Sox" title="Boston Red Sox">Red Sox</a> are the American League leaders in this category with three consecutive titles (<a href="/wiki/2004_World_Series" title="2004 World Series">2004</a>, <a href="/wiki/2007_World_Series" title="2007 World Series">2007</a>, and <a href="/wiki/2013_World_Series" title="2013 World Series">2013</a>) since their last series loss (<a href="/wiki/1986_World_Series" title="1986 World Series">1986</a>).  The Giants lost in <a href="/wiki/2002_World_Series" title="2002 World Series">2002</a> before winning the next three they appeared in (<a href="/wiki/2010_World_Series" title="2010 World Series">2010</a>, <a href="/wiki/2012_World_Series" title="2012 World Series">2012</a>, and <a href="/wiki/2014_World_Series" title="2014 World Series">2014</a>).</li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">Yankees</a> have the most World Series victories (eight) between World Series losses.  After losing the <a href="/wiki/1926_World_Series" title="1926 World Series">1926</a> World Series to the <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Cardinals" title="St. Louis Cardinals">Cardinals</a>, the Yankees won their next eight appearances in the series (<a href="/wiki/1927_World_Series" title="1927 World Series">1927</a>, <a href="/wiki/1928_World_Series" title="1928 World Series">1928</a>, <a href="/wiki/1932_World_Series" title="1932 World Series">1932</a>, <a href="/wiki/1936_World_Series" title="1936 World Series">1936</a>, <a href="/wiki/1937_World_Series" title="1937 World Series">1937</a>, <a href="/wiki/1938_World_Series" title="1938 World Series">1938</a>, <a href="/wiki/1939_World_Series" title="1939 World Series">1939</a>, and <a href="/wiki/1941_World_Series" title="1941 World Series">1941</a>) before losing in <a href="/wiki/1942_World_Series" title="1942 World Series">1942</a> to the Cardinals again.  After this loss, the Yankees went on to win their next seven Series appearances (<a href="/wiki/1943_World_Series" title="1943 World Series">1943</a>, <a href="/wiki/1947_World_Series" title="1947 World Series">1947</a>, <a href="/wiki/1949_World_Series" title="1949 World Series">1949</a>, <a href="/wiki/1950_World_Series" title="1950 World Series">1950</a>, <a href="/wiki/1951_World_Series" title="1951 World Series">1951</a>, <a href="/wiki/1952_World_Series" title="1952 World Series">1952</a>, and <a href="/wiki/1953_World_Series" title="1953 World Series">1953</a>) before their next Series loss in <a href="/wiki/1955_World_Series" title="1955 World Series">1955</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Dodgers" class="mw-redirect" title="Brooklyn Dodgers">Brooklyn Dodgers</a>.  The <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Cardinals" title="St. Louis Cardinals">Cardinals</a> are the National League leader in this category, with four titles (<a href="/wiki/1944_World_Series" title="1944 World Series">1944</a>, <a href="/wiki/1946_World_Series" title="1946 World Series">1946</a>, <a href="/wiki/1964_World_Series" title="1964 World Series">1964</a>, and <a href="/wiki/1967_World_Series" title="1967 World Series">1967</a>) between series losses in 1943 and <a href="/wiki/1968_World_Series" title="1968 World Series">1968</a>.</li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Cubs" title="Chicago Cubs">Cubs</a> and Dodgers are tied at seven apiece for most World Series losses between World Series victories.  The Dodgers lost their first seven appearances in the Fall Classics (<a href="/wiki/1916_World_Series" title="1916 World Series">1916</a>, <a href="/wiki/1920_World_Series" title="1920 World Series">1920</a>, <a href="/wiki/1941_World_Series" title="1941 World Series">1941</a>, <a href="/wiki/1947_World_Series" title="1947 World Series">1947</a>, <a href="/wiki/1949_World_Series" title="1949 World Series">1949</a>, <a href="/wiki/1952_World_Series" title="1952 World Series">1952</a>, and <a href="/wiki/1953_World_Series" title="1953 World Series">1953</a>) before winning their first title in <a href="/wiki/1955_World_Series" title="1955 World Series">1955</a>.  The Cubs\' situation was the opposite: between winning their last two titles (in <a href="/wiki/1908_World_Series" title="1908 World Series">1908</a> and 2016), they lost the World Series in <a href="/wiki/1910_World_Series" title="1910 World Series">1910</a>, <a href="/wiki/1918_World_Series" title="1918 World Series">1918</a>, <a href="/wiki/1929_World_Series" title="1929 World Series">1929</a>, <a href="/wiki/1932_World_Series" title="1932 World Series">1932</a>, <a href="/wiki/1935_World_Series" title="1935 World Series">1935</a>, <a href="/wiki/1938_World_Series" title="1938 World Series">1938</a>, and <a href="/wiki/1945_World_Series" title="1945 World Series">1945</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Indians" title="Cleveland Indians">Cleveland Indians</a> have four World Series losses (<a href="/wiki/1954_World_Series" title="1954 World Series">1954</a>, <a href="/wiki/1995_World_Series" title="1995 World Series">1995</a>, <a href="/wiki/1997_World_Series" title="1997 World Series">1997</a>, and <a href="/wiki/2016_World_Series" title="2016 World Series">2016</a>) since their last crown in <a href="/wiki/1948_World_Series" title="1948 World Series">1948</a>, more than any other team in the American League.</li>\n<li>The longest duration without repeat World Series champions is seventeen years, dating back to the <a href="/wiki/2000_New_York_Yankees_season" title="2000 New York Yankees season">2000 New York Yankees</a>. The previous record of fourteen years (in between the <a href="/wiki/1978_New_York_Yankees_season" title="1978 New York Yankees season">1978 New York Yankees\' win</a> and the <a href="/wiki/1993_Toronto_Blue_Jays_season" title="1993 Toronto Blue Jays season">1993 Toronto Blue Jays\' win</a>) was broken when the <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Giants" title="San Francisco Giants">San Francisco Giants</a> did not qualify for the postseason in 2015 following their victory in the <a href="/wiki/2014_World_Series" title="2014 World Series">2014 World Series</a>.</li>\n<li>The longest sequence of World Series in which each Series was won by a different franchise is 10, from 1978 (Yankees) through 1987 (<a href="/wiki/1987_Minnesota_Twins_season" title="1987 Minnesota Twins season">Minnesota Twins</a>). This streak was broken when the Dodgers, which had won in <a href="/wiki/1981_Los_Angeles_Dodgers_season" title="1981 Los Angeles Dodgers season">1981</a>, won in <a href="/wiki/1988_Los_Angeles_Dodgers_season" title="1988 Los Angeles Dodgers season">1988</a>.</li></ol>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Game-by-game">Game-by-game</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Game-by-game">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<ol><li>Game 7 was won by the home team in the 9 World Series between 1980 and 2013 that went to seven games (the <a href="/wiki/1982_World_Series" title="1982 World Series">1982</a> <a href="/wiki/1982_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="1982 St. Louis Cardinals season">St. Louis Cardinals</a>, <a href="/wiki/1985_World_Series" title="1985 World Series">1985</a> <a href="/wiki/1985_Kansas_City_Royals_season" title="1985 Kansas City Royals season">Kansas City Royals</a>, <a href="/wiki/1986_World_Series" title="1986 World Series">1986</a> <a href="/wiki/1986_New_York_Mets_season" title="1986 New York Mets season">New York Mets</a>, <a href="/wiki/1987_World_Series" title="1987 World Series">1987</a> and <a href="/wiki/1991_World_Series" title="1991 World Series">1991</a> <a href="/wiki/Minnesota_Twins" title="Minnesota Twins">Minnesota Twins</a>, <a href="/wiki/1997_World_Series" title="1997 World Series">1997</a> <a href="/wiki/1997_Florida_Marlins_season" title="1997 Florida Marlins season">Florida Marlins</a>, <a href="/wiki/2001_World_Series" title="2001 World Series">2001</a> <a href="/wiki/Arizona_Diamondbacks" title="Arizona Diamondbacks">Arizona Diamondbacks</a>, <a href="/wiki/2002_World_Series" title="2002 World Series">2002</a> <a href="/wiki/2002_Anaheim_Angels_season" title="2002 Anaheim Angels season">Anaheim Angels</a>, and <a href="/wiki/2011_World_Series" title="2011 World Series">2011</a> <a href="/wiki/2011_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="2011 St. Louis Cardinals season">St. Louis Cardinals</a>) before the Giants won game 7 on the road in <a href="/wiki/2014_World_Series" title="2014 World Series">2014</a>. This trend reverses the previous historical trend in which Game 7 had been most often won by the road team, in <a href="/wiki/1979_World_Series" title="1979 World Series">1979</a>, <a href="/wiki/1975_World_Series" title="1975 World Series">1975</a>, <a href="/wiki/1972_World_Series" title="1972 World Series">1972</a>, <a href="/wiki/1971_World_Series" title="1971 World Series">1971</a>, <a href="/wiki/1968_World_Series" title="1968 World Series">1968</a>, <a href="/wiki/1967_World_Series" title="1967 World Series">1967</a>, <a href="/wiki/1965_World_Series" title="1965 World Series">1965</a>, and <a href="/wiki/1962_World_Series" title="1962 World Series">1962</a>. During the 1960s and 1970s, the home team had won Game 7 only in <a href="/wiki/1960_World_Series" title="1960 World Series">1960</a>, <a href="/wiki/1964_World_Series" title="1964 World Series">1964</a>, and <a href="/wiki/1973_World_Series" title="1973 World Series">1973</a>.</li>\n<li>The greatest comebacks in World Series history were in 1968, when the Detroit Tigers came back from a 3\xe2\x80\x931 game disadvantage to win Game 5 after being behind by 3 runs, before winning games 6 and 7 on the road at St. Louis, and 2016, when the Chicago Cubs scored three runs to win Game 5 and won the last two games in Cleveland.</li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/1981_World_Series" title="1981 World Series">1981</a> <a href="/wiki/1981_Los_Angeles_Dodgers_season" title="1981 Los Angeles Dodgers season">Los Angeles Dodgers</a> are the last team to win a World Series after losing the first two games on the road (against New York). The recent tendency of a team winning the first two games at home and then winning the Series suggests the <i>theoretical</i> advantage to gaining home-field advantage (and the first two games at home).</li>\n<li>The Pittsburgh Pirates won all five of their World Series championships in seven games.</li>\n<li>The Minnesota Twins/Washington Senators won all three of their World Series championships in seven games.</li>\n<li>There have been 19 World Series four-game (4\xe2\x80\x930) sweeps, the most recent of which occurred in 2012.  Nine teams have swept a World Series at least once, the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">Yankees</a> having done so most often (8 times). The <a href="/wiki/Boston_Red_Sox" title="Boston Red Sox">Red Sox</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati_Reds" title="Cincinnati Reds">Reds</a>, and <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Giants" title="San Francisco Giants">Giants</a> have all done it twice. The <a href="/wiki/Atlanta_Braves" title="Atlanta Braves">Braves</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Orioles" title="Baltimore Orioles">Orioles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chicago_White_Sox" title="Chicago White Sox">White Sox</a>, <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Dodgers" title="Los Angeles Dodgers">Dodgers</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Oakland_Athletics" title="Oakland Athletics">Athletics</a> have each swept one Series. Six of these teams (all but the Orioles, Red Sox and White Sox) have also been swept 0\xe2\x80\x934 in at least one World Series. The Red Sox\' two World Series sweeps are the most of any team that has never been swept in one.  The Reds and Yankees are the only teams to have swept each other (the Yankees swept the Reds in <a href="/wiki/1939_World_Series" title="1939 World Series">1939</a>, while the Reds swept the Yankees in <a href="/wiki/1976_World_Series" title="1976 World Series">1976</a>). The Giants are the only team to record World Series sweeps in two cities: New York (<a href="/wiki/1954_World_Series" title="1954 World Series">1954</a>) and San Francisco (<a href="/wiki/2012_World_Series" title="2012 World Series">2012</a>). The <a href="/wiki/1999_World_Series" title="1999 World Series">1999 Yankees</a> are the last team to date, and the only one since <a href="/wiki/1966_World_Series" title="1966 World Series">1966</a>, to sweep a World Series it began on the road (as well as the last American League champion to win a World Series it began on the road until the 2017 season when the Astros defeated the Dodgers in 7 games). The <a href="/wiki/1963_World_Series" title="1963 World Series">1963 Dodgers</a> are the last National League team to date to sweep a World Series it began on the road.</li>\n<li>The Athletics, <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Cardinals" title="St. Louis Cardinals">Cardinals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Cubs" title="Chicago Cubs">Cubs</a>, and Yankees are the only teams to be swept in two World Series. The Athletics and Yankees are the only two of these with at least one World Series sweep to their credit, the other two being among nine teams overall that have never swept a World Series, but have been swept in one (the <a href="/wiki/Detroit_Tigers" title="Detroit Tigers">Tigers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Houston_Astros" title="Houston Astros">Astros</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Indians" title="Cleveland Indians">Indians</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Padres" title="San Diego Padres">Padres</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Phillies" title="Philadelphia Phillies">Phillies</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Pirates" title="Pittsburgh Pirates">Pirates</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Rockies" title="Colorado Rockies">Rockies</a> being the others).</li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/1907_Chicago_Cubs_season" title="1907 Chicago Cubs season">Cubs</a> in <a href="/wiki/1907_World_Series" title="1907 World Series">1907</a> and the <a href="/wiki/1922_New_York_Giants_season" title="1922 New York Giants season">Giants</a> in <a href="/wiki/1922_World_Series" title="1922 World Series">1922</a> won 4 games to 0, but each of those Series\' included a tied game and are not considered to be true sweeps. In 1907, the first game was the tie and the Cubs won four straight after that. In <a href="/wiki/1922_World_Series" title="1922 World Series">1922</a>, Game 2 was the tie.</li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/1976_Cincinnati_Reds_season" title="1976 Cincinnati Reds season">Cincinnati Reds</a> were the only National League team to sweep any World Series between <a href="/wiki/1963_World_Series" title="1963 World Series">1963</a> and <a href="/wiki/2012_World_Series" title="2012 World Series">2012</a>, sweeping their last two series appearances to date in <a href="/wiki/1976_World_Series" title="1976 World Series">1976</a> and <a href="/wiki/1990_World_Series" title="1990 World Series">1990</a>. When added to their Game 7 victory in <a href="/wiki/1975_World_Series" title="1975 World Series">1975</a>, this means that the Reds have won their last 9 consecutive World Series games, making this the current longest winning streak in terms of consecutive World Series games won.  The Reds are also to date the only team since the inception of the League Championship Series (LCS) in 1969 to sweep the entire postseason. The 1976 \xe2\x80\x9cBig Red Machine\xe2\x80\x9d swept the Philadelphia Phillies in the National League LCS in three games, and then swept the New York Yankees in the World Series in four games. The longest ever streak of consecutive World Series games won is 14 by the New York Yankees, who won four straight games to win the <a href="/wiki/1996_World_Series" title="1996 World Series">1996 World Series</a> after losing the first two games of that series, then swept their next two World Series appearances in <a href="/wiki/1998_World_Series" title="1998 World Series">1998</a> and <a href="/wiki/1999_World_Series" title="1999 World Series">1999</a>, and then won the first two games of the <a href="/wiki/2000_World_Series" title="2000 World Series">2000 World Series</a> before losing the third game of that Series to the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Mets" title="New York Mets">New York Mets</a>.</li>\n<li>The only team to have appeared in a World Series and have no wins in a World Series game is the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Rockies" title="Colorado Rockies">Colorado Rockies</a>, who were swept in their only appearance to date in 2007.</li>\n<li>Nine World Series have ended with "walk-off" hits, i.e., that game and the Series ended when the home team won with a base hit in the bottom of the ninth or in extra innings:<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>  <a href="/wiki/1924_World_Series" title="1924 World Series">1924</a>*, <a href="/wiki/1929_World_Series" title="1929 World Series">1929</a>, <a href="/wiki/1935_World_Series" title="1935 World Series">1935</a>, <a href="/wiki/1953_World_Series" title="1953 World Series">1953</a>, <a href="/wiki/1960_World_Series" title="1960 World Series">1960</a>*, <a href="/wiki/1991_World_Series" title="1991 World Series">1991</a>*, <a href="/wiki/1993_World_Series" title="1993 World Series">1993</a>, <a href="/wiki/1997_World_Series" title="1997 World Series">1997</a>*, and <a href="/wiki/2001_World_Series" title="2001 World Series">2001</a>*.  Five of these (marked with a *) were in a deciding Game 7.  In addition, the deciding Game 8 (one game had ended in a tie) of the <a href="/wiki/1912_World_Series" title="1912 World Series">1912 World Series</a> ended in a walk-off <a href="/wiki/Sacrifice_fly" title="Sacrifice fly">sacrifice fly</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>  Two men have ended a World Series with a <a href="/wiki/Walk-off_home_run" title="Walk-off home run">walk-off home run</a>: <a href="/wiki/Bill_Mazeroski" title="Bill Mazeroski">Bill Mazeroski</a> in 1960 and <a href="/wiki/Joe_Carter" title="Joe Carter">Joe Carter</a> in 1993. Mazeroski\'s was a solo shot in the bottom of the ninth of Game 7 to win a championship for the <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Pirates" title="Pittsburgh Pirates">Pittsburgh Pirates</a>, while Carter\'s was a three-run shot in Game 6 that won a championship for the <a href="/wiki/Toronto_Blue_Jays" title="Toronto Blue Jays">Toronto Blue Jays</a>.</li>\n<li>There has been one World Series that ended on a runner caught stealing, on a play that involved three future Hall of Famers.  In the bottom of the ninth inning of Game 7 of the <a href="/wiki/1926_World_Series" title="1926 World Series">1926 World Series</a>, <a href="/wiki/Babe_Ruth" title="Babe Ruth">Babe Ruth</a> of the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">New York Yankees</a> tried to steal second base with two outs and his team trailing the <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Cardinals" title="St. Louis Cardinals">St. Louis Cardinals</a> 3\xe2\x80\x932.  Ruth was thrown out by Cardinals catcher <a href="/wiki/Bob_O%27Farrell" title="Bob O&#39;Farrell">Bob O\'Farrell</a> after <a href="/wiki/Bob_Meusel" title="Bob Meusel">Bob Meusel</a> swung at and missed a pitch from <a href="/wiki/Grover_Cleveland_Alexander" title="Grover Cleveland Alexander">Grover Cleveland Alexander</a>.  St. Louis second baseman <a href="/wiki/Rogers_Hornsby" title="Rogers Hornsby">Rogers Hornsby</a> applied the tag on Ruth, who in his career was successful on 51% of his stolen base attempts.  Ruth, Alexander and Hornsby were inducted into the <a href="/wiki/Baseball_Hall_of_Fame" class="mw-redirect" title="Baseball Hall of Fame">Baseball Hall of Fame</a>.</li>\n<li>One World Series game has ended with a pick-off of a runner.  Kolten Wong of the <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Cardinals" title="St. Louis Cardinals">St. Louis Cardinals</a> was picked off first base in Game 4 of the <a href="/wiki/2013_World_Series" title="2013 World Series">2013 World Series</a> by <a href="/wiki/Boston_Red_Sox" title="Boston Red Sox">Boston Red Sox</a> closer Koji Uehara.  The score was 4\xe2\x80\x932 and rookie Wong was a pinch runner.</li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/2008_Philadelphia_Phillies_season" title="2008 Philadelphia Phillies season">Philadelphia Phillies</a> and the <a href="/wiki/2008_Tampa_Bay_Rays_season" title="2008 Tampa Bay Rays season">Tampa Bay Rays</a> are the first teams to have an elimination game (or <i>any</i> game) be suspended because of weather, and not have it cancelled. Game 5 (in Philadelphia) was suspended on Monday, October 27, 2008 with a 2\xe2\x80\x932 score, and resumed in the bottom of the sixth on Wednesday, October 29.  The Phillies went on to win the game and clinch the series.</li>\n<li>Both of the <a href="/wiki/Minnesota_Twins" title="Minnesota Twins">Minnesota Twins</a>\' World Series titles since relocating to the Twin Cities from Washington, D.C. (where they were the first Washington Senators) were in 7 game series where all games were won by the home team.  The Twins accomplished this in <a href="/wiki/1987_World_Series" title="1987 World Series">1987</a>, when the Twins defeated the St. Louis Cardinals, then 4 years later in <a href="/wiki/1991_World_Series" title="1991 World Series">1991</a>, when the Twins defeated the <a href="/wiki/Atlanta_Braves" title="Atlanta Braves">Atlanta Braves</a>.  The Twins victories in both series were in games 1, 2, 6, and 7, while their National League opponents won games 3, 4, and 5.  This same scenario also occurred in <a href="/wiki/2001_World_Series" title="2001 World Series">2001</a>, when the Arizona Diamondbacks defeated the New York Yankees.</li>\n<li>Also of note when it comes to the three series where every game was won by the home team, a pitcher was MVP.  In the <a href="/wiki/1987_World_Series" title="1987 World Series">1987 World Series</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frank_Viola" title="Frank Viola">Frank Viola</a> was the MVP having pitched games 1, 4, and 7, and finishing with a 2\xe2\x80\x931 record.  In <a href="/wiki/1991_World_Series" title="1991 World Series">1991</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jack_Morris" title="Jack Morris">Jack Morris</a> achieved the same feat pitching games 1, 4, and 7 with a 2\xe2\x80\x930 record and a no decision in game 4, and winning MVP honors.  However, Morris\'s MVP came on the heels of pitching 10 shutout innings in game 7.  Finally, in <a href="/wiki/2001_World_Series" title="2001 World Series">2001</a>, <a href="/wiki/Curt_Schilling" title="Curt Schilling">Curt Schilling</a> and <a href="/wiki/Randy_Johnson" title="Randy Johnson">Randy Johnson</a> took MVP honors by being the reason the <a href="/wiki/2001_Arizona_Diamondbacks_season" title="2001 Arizona Diamondbacks season">Arizona Diamondbacks</a> were in position to win the series.</li>\n<li>The Boston Red Sox have lost 4 World Series, all in 7 games. (1946, 1967, 1975, &amp; 1986)</li>\n<li>Four World Series ended with teams clinching the championship in the final game of the series which was not a game 7 and went into extra innings. The title was won this way in 1939, <a href="/wiki/1992_World_Series" title="1992 World Series">1992</a>, 2012, and 2015, with the road team winning each time.</li>\n<li>The home team has not won a deciding game of a World Series since <a href="/wiki/2013_World_Series" title="2013 World Series">2013</a>, and has not done so in five of the last six seasons.</li>\n<li>The winning team has scored fewer runs (composite) on 22 occasions, six of these in six-game series: <a href="/wiki/1918_World_Series#Composite_box" title="1918 World Series">1918</a>, <a href="/wiki/1959_World_Series#Composite_line_score" title="1959 World Series">1959</a>, <a href="/wiki/1977_World_Series#Series_statistics" title="1977 World Series">1977</a>, <a href="/wiki/1992_World_Series#Composite_box" title="1992 World Series">1992</a>, <a href="/wiki/1996_World_Series#Composite_box" title="1996 World Series">1996</a>, and <a href="/wiki/2003_World_Series#Composite_box" title="2003 World Series">2003</a>. Seven-game series winners were outscored in <a href="/wiki/1912_World_Series#Composite_line_score" title="1912 World Series">1912</a>, <a href="/wiki/1924_World_Series#Composite_line_score" title="1924 World Series">1924</a>, <a href="/wiki/1925_World_Series#Composite_line_score" title="1925 World Series">1925</a>, <a href="/wiki/1931_World_Series#Composite_line_score" title="1931 World Series">1931</a>, <a href="/wiki/1940_World_Series#Composite_line_score" title="1940 World Series">1940</a>, <a href="/wiki/1957_World_Series#Composite_line_score" title="1957 World Series">1957</a>, <a href="/wiki/1960_World_Series#Composite_box" title="1960 World Series">1960</a>, <a href="/wiki/1962_World_Series#Composite_box" title="1962 World Series">1962</a>, <a href="/wiki/1964_World_Series#Composite_box" title="1964 World Series">1964</a>, <a href="/wiki/1971_World_Series#Composite_box" title="1971 World Series">1971</a>, <a href="/wiki/1972_World_Series#Composite_box" title="1972 World Series">1972</a>, <a href="/wiki/1973_World_Series#Composite_line_score" title="1973 World Series">1973</a>, <a href="/wiki/1975_World_Series#Composite_line_score" title="1975 World Series">1975</a>, <a href="/wiki/1991_World_Series#Composite_line_score" title="1991 World Series">1991</a>, <a href="/wiki/1997_World_Series#Composite_box" title="1997 World Series">1997</a>, and <a href="/wiki/2002_World_Series#Composite_box" title="2002 World Series">2002</a>. An equal number of runs were scored by the teams in <a href="/wiki/1948_World_Series#Composite_box" title="1948 World Series">1948</a> (6 games), <a href="/wiki/2016_World_Series#Composite_line_score" title="2016 World Series">2016</a>, and <a href="/wiki/2017_World_Series#Composite_line_score" title="2017 World Series">2017</a>. A five-game series winner has yet to be outscored: the closest margins were two runs in <a href="/wiki/1915_World_Series#Composite_line_score" title="1915 World Series">1915</a> and three in <a href="/wiki/2000_World_Series#Composite_box" title="2000 World Series">2000</a>. The closest composite margin in a four-game sweep is six runs (<a href="/wiki/1950_World_Series#Composite_box" title="1950 World Series">1950</a>, <a href="/wiki/2005_World_Series#Series_statistics" title="2005 World Series">2005</a>).</li></ol>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_rivalries">Local rivalries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Local rivalries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_rivalries" title="Major League Baseball rivalries">Major League Baseball rivalries</a></div>\n<p>When two teams share the same state or metropolitan area, fans often develop strong loyalties to one and antipathies towards the other, sometimes building on already-existing rivalries between cities or neighborhoods. Before the introduction of <a href="/wiki/Interleague_play" title="Interleague play">interleague play</a> in 1997, the only opportunity for two teams playing in the same area but in different leagues to face each other in official competition would have been in a World Series.\n</p>\n<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Cross-town_Series">Cross-town Series</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Cross-town Series">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>\n<p>The first city to host an entire World Series was Chicago in <a href="/wiki/1906_World_Series" title="1906 World Series">1906</a>.  The <a href="/wiki/1906_Chicago_White_Sox_season" title="1906 Chicago White Sox season">Chicago White Sox</a> were known as "the Hitless Wonders" that year, with the worst team batting average in the American League.  The <a href="/wiki/1906_Chicago_Cubs_season" title="1906 Chicago Cubs season">Chicago Cubs</a> had a winning percentage of .763, a record that still stands.  But in an upset, the White Sox beat the Cubs four games to two.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Fourteen "<a href="/wiki/Subway_Series" title="Subway Series">Subway Series</a>" have been played entirely within New York City, all including the American League\'s <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">New York Yankees</a>. Thirteen of them matched the Yankees with either the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Giants_(NL)" class="mw-redirect" title="New York Giants (NL)">New York Giants</a> or the <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Dodgers" class="mw-redirect" title="Brooklyn Dodgers">Brooklyn Dodgers</a> of the National League. The initial instances occurred in <a href="/wiki/1921_World_Series" title="1921 World Series">1921</a> and <a href="/wiki/1922_World_Series" title="1922 World Series">1922</a>, when the Giants beat the Yankees in consecutive World Series that were not technically "subway series" since the teams shared the <a href="/wiki/Polo_Grounds" title="Polo Grounds">Polo Grounds</a> as their home ballpark. The Yankees finally beat the Giants <a href="/wiki/1923_World_Series" title="1923 World Series">the following year</a>, their first in their brand-new <a href="/wiki/Yankee_Stadium_(1923)" title="Yankee Stadium (1923)">Yankee Stadium</a>, and won the two teams\' three subsequent Fall Classic match-ups in <a href="/wiki/1936_World_Series" title="1936 World Series">1936</a>, <a href="/wiki/1937_World_Series" title="1937 World Series">1937</a> and <a href="/wiki/1951_World_Series" title="1951 World Series">1951</a>. The Yankees faced Brooklyn seven times in October, winning their first five meetings in <a href="/wiki/1941_World_Series" title="1941 World Series">1941</a>, <a href="/wiki/1947_World_Series" title="1947 World Series">1947</a>, <a href="/wiki/1949_World_Series" title="1949 World Series">1949</a>, <a href="/wiki/1952_World_Series" title="1952 World Series">1952</a> and <a href="/wiki/1953_World_Series" title="1953 World Series">1953</a>, before losing to the Dodgers in <a href="/wiki/1955_World_Series" title="1955 World Series">1955</a>, Brooklyn\'s sole World Championship. The last Subway Series involving the original New York ballclubs came in <a href="/wiki/1956_World_Series" title="1956 World Series">1956</a>, when the Yankees again beat the Dodgers. The trio was separated in 1958 when the Dodgers and Giants moved to California (although the Yankees subsequently met and beat the now-<a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Giants" title="San Francisco Giants">San Francisco Giants</a> in <a href="/wiki/1962_World_Series" title="1962 World Series">1962</a>, and played the now-<a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Dodgers" title="Los Angeles Dodgers">Los Angeles Dodgers</a> four times, losing to them in a four-game sweep in <a href="/wiki/1963_World_Series" title="1963 World Series">1963</a>, beating them back-to-back in <a href="/wiki/1977_World_Series" title="1977 World Series">1977</a> and <a href="/wiki/1978_World_Series" title="1978 World Series">1978</a> and losing to them in <a href="/wiki/1981_World_Series" title="1981 World Series">1981</a>). An all-New York Series did not recur until <a href="/wiki/2000_World_Series" title="2000 World Series">2000</a>, when the <a href="/wiki/2000_New_York_Yankees_season" title="2000 New York Yankees season">Yankees</a> defeated the <a href="/wiki/2000_New_York_Mets_season" title="2000 New York Mets season">New York Mets</a> in five games.\n</p><p>The last World Series played entirely in one ballpark was the <a href="/wiki/1944_World_Series" title="1944 World Series">1944 "Streetcar Series"</a> between the <a href="/wiki/1944_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="1944 St. Louis Cardinals season">St. Louis Cardinals</a> and the <a href="/wiki/1944_St._Louis_Browns_season" title="1944 St. Louis Browns season">St. Louis Browns</a>. The Cardinals won in six games, all held in their shared home, <a href="/wiki/Sportsman%27s_Park" title="Sportsman&#39;s Park">Sportsman\'s Park</a>.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/1989_World_Series" title="1989 World Series">1989 World Series</a>, sometimes called the "<a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_%E2%80%93_Oakland_Bay_Bridge" class="mw-redirect" title="San Francisco \xe2\x80\x93 Oakland Bay Bridge">Bay Bridge</a> Series" or the "<a href="/wiki/Bay_Area_Rapid_Transit" title="Bay Area Rapid Transit">BART</a> Series" (after the connecting transit line), featured the <a href="/wiki/Oakland_Athletics" title="Oakland Athletics">Oakland Athletics</a> and the <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Giants" title="San Francisco Giants">San Francisco Giants</a>, teams that play just across <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Bay" title="San Francisco Bay">San Francisco Bay</a> from each other. The series is most remembered for the <a href="/wiki/1989_Loma_Prieta_earthquake" title="1989 Loma Prieta earthquake">major earthquake</a> that struck the <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Bay_Area" title="San Francisco Bay Area">San Francisco Bay Area</a> just before game 3 was scheduled to begin. The quake caused significant damage to both communities and <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco%E2%80%93Oakland_Bay_Bridge#Earthquake_damage_and_subsequent_upgrades" title="San Francisco\xe2\x80\x93Oakland Bay Bridge">severed the Bay Bridge</a> that connects them, forcing the postponement of the series. Play resumed ten days later, and the A\'s swept the Giants in four games. (The earthquake disruption of the Series almost completely overshadowed the fact that the 1989 Series represented a resumption after many decades of the October rivalry between the Giants and the A\'s dating back to the early years of the 20th Century, when the then-New York Giants had defeated the then-<a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Athletics" class="mw-redirect" title="Philadelphia Athletics">Philadelphia Athletics</a> in <a href="/wiki/1905_World_Series" title="1905 World Series">1905</a>, and had lost to them in <a href="/wiki/1911_World_Series" title="1911 World Series">1911</a> and again in <a href="/wiki/1913_World_Series" title="1913 World Series">1913</a>.)\n</p><p>The Giants are the only team to have played in cross-town World Series in two cities, having faced the Yankees six times while located in New York, and the Athletics once while based in San Francisco.\n</p><p>Two cross-town World Series match-ups were formerly possible but did not occur \xe2\x80\x94 the Boston Red Sox vs. the Boston Braves, and the Philadelphia Phillies vs. the Philadelphia Athletics.  (The Braves moved to Milwaukee in 1953, and the Athletics moved to Kansas City in 1955.)\n</p><p>Currently there are four metropolitan areas that have two Major League Baseball teams \xe2\x80\x94 New York, Chicago, San Francisco, and Los Angeles.  Of the four, only Los Angeles has not hosted a cross-town World Series.  Such a contest would pit the Dodgers against the Angels.\n</p><p>Below is a chronological list of World Series played between teams from the same metropolitan area, with the winning teams listed in <b>boldface</b>.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="font-size: 90%;">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Year</th>\n<th>American League</th>\n<th>National League\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a Yankees</td>\n<td><b>New York Giants</b>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/1923_World_Series" title="1923 World Series">1923</a></td>\n<td><b>New York Yankees</b></td>\n<td>New York Giants\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/1936_World_Series" title="1936 World Series">1936</a></td>\n<td><b>New York Yankees</b></td>\n<td>New York Giants\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a
