Browns</td>\n<td><b>St. Louis Cardinals</b>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/1947_World_Series" title="1947 World Series">1947</a></td>\n<td><b>New York Yankees</b></td>\n<td>Brooklyn Dodgers\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/1949_World_Series" title="1949 World Series">1949</a></td>\n<td><b>New York Yankees</b></td>\n<td>Brooklyn Dodgers\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/1951_World_Series" title="1951 World Series">1951</a></td>\n<td><b>New York Yankees</b></td>\n<td>New York Giants\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/1952_World_Series" title="1952 World Series">1952</a></td>\n<td><b>New York Yankees</b></td>\n<td>Brooklyn Dodgers\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/1953_World_Series" title="1953 World Series">1953</a></td>\n<td><b>New York Yankees</b></td>\n<td>Brooklyn Dodgers\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/1955_World_Series" title="1955 World Series">1955</a></td>\n<td>New York Yankees</td>\n<td><b>Brooklyn Dodgers</b>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/1956_World_Series" title="1956 World Series">1956</a></td>\n<td><b>New York Yankees</b></td>\n<td>Brooklyn Dodgers\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/1989_World_Series" title="1989 World Series">1989</a></td>\n<td><b>Oakland Athletics</b></td>\n<td>San Francisco Giants\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/2000_World_Series" title="2000 World Series">2000</a></td>\n<td><b>New York Yankees</b></td>\n<td>New York Mets\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Cross-state_rivalries">Cross-state rivalries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Cross-state rivalries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>\n<p>The historic rivalry between <a href="/wiki/Northern_California" title="Northern California">Northern</a> and <a href="/wiki/Southern_California" title="Southern California">Southern California</a> added to the interest in the Oakland Athletics-<a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Dodgers" title="Los Angeles Dodgers">Los Angeles Dodgers</a> series in <a href="/wiki/1974_World_Series" title="1974 World Series">1974</a> and <a href="/wiki/1988_World_Series" title="1988 World Series">1988</a> and in the San Francisco Giants\' series against the then-<a href="/wiki/Anaheim_Angels" class="mw-redirect" title="Anaheim Angels">Anaheim Angels</a> in <a href="/wiki/2002_World_Series" title="2002 World Series">2002</a>.\n</p><p>Other than the St. Louis World Series of 1944, the only postseason tournament held entirely within <a href="/wiki/Missouri" title="Missouri">Missouri</a> was the <a href="/wiki/1985_World_Series" title="1985 World Series">I-70 Series</a> in 1985 (named for the <a href="/wiki/Interstate_70" title="Interstate 70">Interstate Highway</a> <a href="/wiki/Interstate_70_in_Missouri" title="Interstate 70 in Missouri">connecting the two cities</a>) between the <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Cardinals" title="St. Louis Cardinals">St. Louis Cardinals</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Kansas_City_Royals" title="Kansas City Royals">Kansas City Royals</a>, who won at home in the seventh game.\n</p><p>Going into the 2017 season, there has never been an in-state World Series between the teams in Ohio (<a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Indians" title="Cleveland Indians">Cleveland Indians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati_Reds" title="Cincinnati Reds">Cincinnati Reds</a>), Florida (<a href="/wiki/Tampa_Bay_Rays" title="Tampa Bay Rays">Tampa Bay Rays</a> and <a href="/wiki/Miami_Marlins" title="Miami Marlins">Miami Marlins</a>), Texas (<a href="/wiki/Texas_Rangers_(baseball)" title="Texas Rangers (baseball)">Texas Rangers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Houston_Astros" title="Houston Astros">Houston Astros</a> \xe2\x80\x93 who now both play in the American League since the Astros changed leagues in 2013,  making any future joint World Series appearance an impossibility unless one of the teams switches leagues), or Pennsylvania (the <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Phillies" title="Philadelphia Phillies">Philadelphia Phillies</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Pirates" title="Pittsburgh Pirates">Pittsburgh Pirates</a> have been traditional National League rivals going back to the late 19th Century). Neither the Phillies nor the Pirates ever faced the Athletics in October during the latter team\'s tenure in Philadelphia, through 1954.  The <a href="/wiki/Boston_Red_Sox" title="Boston Red Sox">Boston Red Sox</a> never similarly faced the <a href="/wiki/Atlanta_Braves" title="Atlanta Braves">Braves</a> while the latter team played in Boston through 1952.  There also was never an all-Canada World Series between the <a href="/wiki/Toronto_Blue_Jays" title="Toronto Blue Jays">Toronto Blue Jays</a> and the former <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Expos" title="Montreal Expos">Montreal Expos</a>, who never won a National League pennant when they played in that Canadian city from 1969 through 2004. The Expos became the <a href="/wiki/Washington_Nationals" title="Washington Nationals">Washington Nationals</a> in 2005 \xe2\x80\x93 raising the possibility of a potential future "<a href="/wiki/Interstate_95" title="Interstate 95">I-95</a> World Series" between the National League team and the AL\'s <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Orioles" title="Baltimore Orioles">Baltimore Orioles</a>, who play just 50 miles to the north of Washington. Finally, the Los Angeles and/or Anaheim Angels have never faced off in October against either the Dodgers or against the <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Padres" title="San Diego Padres">San Diego Padres</a> for bragging rights in Southern California, although all three of those teams have appeared in the World Series at various times.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Pennants_won_in_different_cities">Pennants won in different cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Pennants won in different cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<ol><li>The <a href="/wiki/Atlanta_Braves" title="Atlanta Braves">Braves</a> are the only team to have both won and lost a World Series in three home cities (Boston, Milwaukee, and Atlanta).</li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/Oakland_Athletics" title="Oakland Athletics">Athletics</a> have had three home cities (Philadelphia, Kansas City, and Oakland), but have appeared in the World Series (both winning and losing) while based in only two of them (Philadelphia and Oakland).</li>\n<li>Three other teams have both won and lost the Fall Classic in two home cities: The <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Dodgers" title="Los Angeles Dodgers">Dodgers</a> (Brooklyn and Los Angeles), the <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Giants" title="San Francisco Giants">Giants</a> (New York and San Francisco), and the <a href="/wiki/Minnesota_Twins" title="Minnesota Twins">Twins</a> (the Twin Cities and Washington, D.C., as the first Senators).</li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Orioles" title="Baltimore Orioles">Orioles</a> are the only other team to have played in the World Series in two home cities (Baltimore and St. Louis, as the Browns), but all three of their titles (and three of their four losses) have come while based in Baltimore.</li></ol>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="The_original_sixteen_teams">The original sixteen teams</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: The original sixteen teams">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>At the time the first modern World Series began in 1903, each league had eight clubs, all of which survive today (although sometimes in a different city or with a new nickname), comprising the "original sixteen".\n</p>\n<ol><li>Every original team has won at least two World Series titles. The <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Phillies" title="Philadelphia Phillies">Philadelphia Phillies</a> (National League) were the last of the original teams to win their first Series, in <a href="/wiki/1980_World_Series" title="1980 World Series">1980</a>. They were also the last to win at least two, with their second Series victory in <a href="/wiki/2008_World_Series" title="2008 World Series">2008</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Cubs" title="Chicago Cubs">Cubs</a> were the first team to win the series twice, in 1907 and 1908.</li>\n<li>The last original American League team to win its first World Series was the <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Orioles" title="Baltimore Orioles">Baltimore Orioles</a> (former <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_St._Louis_Browns" title="History of the St. Louis Browns">St. Louis Browns</a>, originally the Milwaukee Brewers), winning in <a href="/wiki/1966_World_Series" title="1966 World Series">1966</a>.</li>\n<li>The Orioles were also the last original team in the majors to make their first World Series appearance, as the St. Louis Browns in <a href="/wiki/1944_World_Series" title="1944 World Series">1944</a>. Although they never won another American League pennant while in St. Louis, they have won three World Series in six appearances since moving to Baltimore. The <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Cardinals" title="St. Louis Cardinals">St. Louis Cardinals</a> were the last original National League team to appear in or win a modern World Series, doing both in <a href="/wiki/1926_World_Series" title="1926 World Series">1926</a>. They have subsequently won more World Series than any other National League club: 11 championships through 2017.</li>\n<li>The New York Yankees have defeated all eight original NL teams in a World Series. Conversely, they have lost at least one World Series to six of the original NL teams, never losing to the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Cubs" title="Chicago Cubs">Chicago Cubs</a> or the <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Phillies" title="Philadelphia Phillies">Philadelphia Phillies</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Boston_Red_Sox" title="Boston Red Sox">Boston Red Sox</a> have played at least one Series against every original National League team <i>except</i> the (Boston, Milwaukee and Atlanta) <a href="/wiki/Atlanta_Braves" title="Atlanta Braves">Braves</a>, with whom they shared a home city through 1952.</li>\n<li>The St. Louis Cardinals are currently the only club of the National League\'s original eight that holds an overall Series lead over the Yankees, 3 to 2, taking that lead in 1964.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> The Giants won their first two Series over the Yankees (1921 and 1922), but the Yankees have faced the Giants five times since then and have won all five, taking the overall lead over the Giants in 1937.  The Pittsburgh Pirates and Yankees have faced each other twice (1927 and 1960), with the Yankees winning in 1927 and the Pirates winning in 1960, making the two teams .500 against each other.</li>\n<li>Since the two leagues expanded beyond eight teams apiece in 1961, the American League\'s <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Indians" title="Cleveland Indians">Cleveland Indians</a> are the only original team that has not won a World Series against the larger field of competitors.</li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/2015_World_Series" title="2015 World Series">2015 World Series</a> was the first ever, and to date only, World Series to not feature any of the original sixteen teams.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup></li></ol>\n<h4><span id="Expansion_teams_.28after_1960.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Expansion_teams_(after_1960)">Expansion teams (after 1960)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Expansion teams (after 1960)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<ol><li>The <a href="/wiki/2001_World_Series" title="2001 World Series">2001</a> <a href="/wiki/Arizona_Diamondbacks" title="Arizona Diamondbacks">Arizona Diamondbacks</a> won their first pennant and World Series in fewer seasons than any other expansion team (both attained in their 4th season). The <a href="/wiki/1997_World_Series" title="1997 World Series">1997 World Series Champion</a> <a href="/wiki/Miami_Marlins" title="Miami Marlins">Florida Marlins</a> achieved these milestones in the second-fewest number of seasons (fifth season). The fastest AL expansion franchise to win a pennant was the <a href="/wiki/Tampa_Bay_Rays" title="Tampa Bay Rays">Tampa Bay Rays</a> in 2008 (11th season) and the fastest AL expansion franchise to win a World Series was the <a href="/wiki/Toronto_Blue_Jays" title="Toronto Blue Jays">Toronto Blue Jays</a> in 1992 (16th season).</li>\n<li>While the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Mets" title="New York Mets">New York Mets</a> (NL) were the first expansion team to win or appear in the World Series (doing both in 1969), the American League would have to wait until <a href="/wiki/1980_World_Series" title="1980 World Series">1980</a> for its first expansion-team World Series appearance, and until <a href="/wiki/1985_World_Series" title="1985 World Series">1985</a> for its first expansion-team win. Both were by the <a href="/wiki/Kansas_City_Royals" title="Kansas City Royals">Kansas City Royals</a>.  The AL also had two expansion teams appear in the World Series (the <a href="/wiki/Milwaukee_Brewers" title="Milwaukee Brewers">Milwaukee Brewers</a> being the second, in <a href="/wiki/1982_World_Series" title="1982 World Series">1982</a>) before the National League\'s second expansion team to appear\xe2\x80\x94the <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Padres" title="San Diego Padres">San Diego Padres</a> in <a href="/wiki/1984_World_Series" title="1984 World Series">1984</a>.</li>\n<li>With the <a href="/wiki/2015_New_York_Mets_season" title="2015 New York Mets season">New York Mets</a> defeating the <a href="/wiki/2015_Chicago_Cubs_season" title="2015 Chicago Cubs season">Chicago Cubs</a> in a four-game sweep in the <a href="/wiki/2015_National_League_Championship_Series" title="2015 National League Championship Series">2015 National League Championship Series</a> and the <a href="/wiki/2015_Kansas_City_Royals_season" title="2015 Kansas City Royals season">Kansas City Royals</a> defeating the <a href="/wiki/2015_Toronto_Blue_Jays_season" title="2015 Toronto Blue Jays season">Toronto Blue Jays</a> in six games in the <a href="/wiki/2015_American_League_Championship_Series" title="2015 American League Championship Series">2015 American League Championship Series</a>, the <a href="/wiki/2015_World_Series" title="2015 World Series">2015 World Series</a> became the first ever World Series matchup in which both teams were expansion teams, where the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Mets" title="New York Mets">Mets</a> (whose first season occurred in 1962) faced off against the <a href="/wiki/Kansas_City_Royals" title="Kansas City Royals">Kansas City Royals</a> (whose first season occurred in 1969), with the Royals winning in five games.  Until 2015, all World Series matchups featured at least one of the 16 teams established by 1903.</li>\n<li>In the first World Series to only have expansion teams, the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Mets" title="New York Mets">New York Mets</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Kansas_City_Royals" title="Kansas City Royals">Kansas City Royals</a> were each the first expansion team in each respective league to appear in the World Series, the Mets in 1969 and the Royals in 1980.  Each team was also the first team in each respective league to win the World Series, the Mets in 1969 and the Royals in 1985.  Each team has the most appearance by an expansion team in each respective league in the World Series, with five for the Mets in 1969, 1973, 1986, 2000, and 2015, and four for the Royals in 1980, 1985, 2014, and 2015.</li>\n<li>12 expansion teams have now played in at least one Series.  As of the end of the 2017 edition, expansion teams were 11\xe2\x80\x9312 in the World Series, with four teams (the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Mets" title="New York Mets">New York Mets</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kansas_City_Royals" title="Kansas City Royals">Kansas City Royals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Toronto_Blue_Jays" title="Toronto Blue Jays">Toronto Blue Jays</a> and <a href="/wiki/Miami_Marlins" title="Miami Marlins">Miami Marlins</a>) each winning two. The then-<a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Angels_of_Anaheim" class="mw-redirect" title="Los Angeles Angels of Anaheim">Anaheim Angels</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Arizona_Diamondbacks" title="Arizona Diamondbacks">Arizona Diamondbacks</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Houston_Astros" title="Houston Astros">Houston Astros</a> had each won one Series by the end of the 2017 season.</li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/Toronto_Blue_Jays" title="Toronto Blue Jays">Toronto Blue Jays</a> (1992 and 1993), <a href="/wiki/Miami_Marlins" title="Miami Marlins">Miami Marlins</a> (1997 and 2003 as the Florida Marlins), <a href="/wiki/Arizona_Diamondbacks" title="Arizona Diamondbacks">Arizona Diamondbacks</a> (2001) and <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Angels_of_Anaheim" class="mw-redirect" title="Los Angeles Angels of Anaheim">Los Angeles Angels</a> (2002 as the Anaheim Angels) have never lost a World Series appearance.</li>\n<li>Five expansion teams have appeared in the World Series without ever winning a championship: twice for the <a href="/wiki/Texas_Rangers_(baseball)" title="Texas Rangers (baseball)">Texas Rangers</a> (formerly the second Washington Senators) and <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Padres" title="San Diego Padres">San Diego Padres</a>, and once each for the <a href="/wiki/Milwaukee_Brewers" title="Milwaukee Brewers">Milwaukee Brewers</a> (formerly Seattle Pilots), <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Rockies" title="Colorado Rockies">Colorado Rockies</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tampa_Bay_Rays" title="Tampa Bay Rays">Tampa Bay Rays</a> (formerly Devil Rays).</li>\n<li>Two expansion teams have not yet won a league pennant (and therefore also have not appeared in a World Series): the American League\'s <a href="/wiki/Seattle_Mariners" title="Seattle Mariners">Seattle Mariners</a> and the National League\'s <a href="/wiki/Washington_Nationals" title="Washington Nationals">Washington Nationals</a> (formerly Montreal Expos).  Both teams have competed in postseason play and appeared in their respective League Championship Series at least once, but have no League Championship Series victories.</li></ol>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_notes">Other notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Other notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<ol><li>The team with the better regular season winning percentage has won the World Series 53 times, or 48.18% (53 of 110) of the time.  Three World Series have featured teams with identical regular season records (1949, 1958, 2013).</li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/Toronto_Blue_Jays" title="Toronto Blue Jays">Toronto Blue Jays</a> are the only Canadian team ever to win a pennant or a World Series, doing both twice, in <a href="/wiki/1992_World_Series" title="1992 World Series">1992</a> and <a href="/wiki/1993_World_Series" title="1993 World Series">1993</a>.</li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Cubs" title="Chicago Cubs">Chicago Cubs</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Houston_Astros" title="Houston Astros">Houston Astros</a> are the only teams with a World Series title that have never clinched one at home.</li>\n<li>Three series have matched up the previous two World Champions, with the New York Yankees winning all three. The <a href="/wiki/1928_World_Series" title="1928 World Series">1928 World Series</a> was contested by the 1926 champion Cardinals and 1927 champion Yankees; the Yankees won the series 4\xe2\x80\x930. In 1943, the 1941 champion Yankees met the 1942 champion Cardinals, which the Yankees won 4\xe2\x80\x931.  In the <a href="/wiki/1958_World_Series" title="1958 World Series">1958 World Series</a>, the 1956 champion Yankees faced the 1957 champion Milwaukee Braves; the Yankees won this series 4\xe2\x80\x933. The <a href="/wiki/2012_National_League_Championship_Series" title="2012 National League Championship Series">2012 National League Championship Series</a> also matched up the previous two World Champions: the 2010 champion Giants and the 2011 champion Cardinals; the Giants won this series 4\xe2\x80\x933.</li>\n<li>As of the present, there are two World Series that cannot have a rematch, the <a href="/wiki/1982_World_Series" title="1982 World Series">1982 World Series</a> between the NL champion <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Cardinals" title="St. Louis Cardinals">St. Louis Cardinals</a> and AL champion <a href="/wiki/Milwaukee_Brewers" title="Milwaukee Brewers">Milwaukee Brewers</a> and the <a href="/wiki/2005_World_Series" title="2005 World Series">2005 World Series</a> between the AL champion <a href="/wiki/Chicago_White_Sox" title="Chicago White Sox">Chicago White Sox</a> and NL champion <a href="/wiki/Houston_Astros" title="Houston Astros">Houston Astros</a>.  The Brewers, who were inaugurated by the American League as the Seattle Pilots in 1969 and relocated to Milwaukee in 1970, were moved to the NL starting in 1998.  The Astros, who were inaugurated by the National League in 1962 as the Houston Colt .45s and adopted their current name in 1965, were moved to the AL starting in 2013.  Therefore, the latest postseason round where the Brewers could face the Cardinals today would be in the National League Championship Series (which has occurred once, in 2011) while the latest postseason round where the Astros could face the White Sox today would be in the American League Championship Series (has never occurred).</li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/Milwaukee_Brewers" title="Milwaukee Brewers">Milwaukee Brewers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Houston_Astros" title="Houston Astros">Houston Astros</a> are the only two teams in MLB to have played in both the <a href="/wiki/American_League_Championship_Series" title="American League Championship Series">American League Championship Series</a> (ALCS) and <a href="/wiki/National_League_Championship_Series" title="National League Championship Series">National League Championship Series</a> (NLCS).  The Brewers won their lone ALCS appearance in 1982 against the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Angels" title="Los Angeles Angels">then-California Angels</a> and lost both of their NLCS appearances in 2011 against the <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Cardinals" title="St. Louis Cardinals">St. Louis Cardinals</a>, and in 2018 against the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Dodgers" title="Los Angeles Dodgers">Los Angeles Dodgers</a>, making them 1\xe2\x80\x932 all time between both League Championship Series.  The Astros, meanwhile, have a 2\xe2\x80\x934 record between both League Championship Series, having gone 1\xe2\x80\x933 in four NLCS appearances (lost in 1980 to the <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Phillies" title="Philadelphia Phillies">Philadelphia Phillies</a>, lost in 1986 to the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Mets" title="New York Mets">New York Mets</a>, lost in 2004 to the Cardinals, and won in 2005 versus the Cardinals) and 1-1 in their ALCS appearances against the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">New York Yankees</a> in 2017 and the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Red_Sox" title="Boston Red Sox">Boston Red Sox</a> in 2018 (a victory in seven against the Yankees and a loss in five games against the Red Sox).  With their victories in both the <a href="/wiki/2005_National_League_Championship_Series" title="2005 National League Championship Series">2005 National League Championship Series</a> and the <a href="/wiki/2017_American_League_Championship_Series" title="2017 American League Championship Series">2017 American League Championship Series</a>, the Astros are the only team in MLB to have represented both the <a href="/wiki/National_League" title="National League">National League</a> and the <a href="/wiki/American_League" title="American League">American League</a> in the World Series.</li>\n<li>The 2015 World Series game 1 between the New York Mets and the Kansas City Royals was the longest game 1 in history at 5 hours and 9 minutes.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Yogi_Berra" title="Yogi Berra">Yogi Berra</a> of the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">New York Yankees</a> holds the record for most World Series championships by a player with 10.   <a href="/wiki/Joe_DiMaggio" title="Joe DiMaggio">Joe DiMaggio</a> of the Yankees is second with 9.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Joe_McCarthy_(manager)" title="Joe McCarthy (manager)">Joe McCarthy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Casey_Stengel" title="Casey Stengel">Casey Stengel</a> are tied for the most World Series titles by a manager with 7 apiece, all 14 of them with the Yankees.   <a href="/wiki/Connie_Mack" title="Connie Mack">Connie Mack</a> managed the Philadelphia Athletics to 5 World Series crowns.</li>\n<li>The all-time World Series single-game attendance record is 92,706, set in Game 5 of the <a href="/wiki/1959_World_Series" title="1959 World Series">1959 World Series</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Memorial_Coliseum" title="Los Angeles Memorial Coliseum">Los Angeles Memorial Coliseum</a>, the temporary home of the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Dodgers" title="Los Angeles Dodgers">Los Angeles Dodgers</a> until <a href="/wiki/Dodger_Stadium" title="Dodger Stadium">Dodger Stadium</a> opened in 1962.  The <a href="/wiki/Chicago_White_Sox" title="Chicago White Sox">Chicago White Sox</a> defeated the Dodgers 1\xe2\x80\x930 in the record-setting game.  Games 3 and 4 of that series also drew crowds in excess of 92,000.</li></ol>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Television_coverage_and_ratings">Television coverage and ratings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Television coverage and ratings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_World_Series_broadcasters" title="List of World Series broadcasters">List of World Series broadcasters</a> and <a href="/wiki/World_Series_television_ratings" title="World Series television ratings">World Series television ratings</a></div>\n<p>When the World Series was first broadcast on television in <a href="/wiki/1947_World_Series" title="1947 World Series">1947</a>, it was only televised to a few surrounding areas via coaxial inter-connected stations: New York City (<a href="/wiki/WNBC" title="WNBC">WNBT</a>); <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a> (<a href="/wiki/KYW-TV" title="KYW-TV">WPTZ</a>); <a href="/wiki/Schenectady,_New_York" title="Schenectady, New York">Schenectady</a>/<a href="/wiki/Albany,_New_York" title="Albany, New York">Albany, New York</a> (<a href="/wiki/WRGB" title="WRGB">WRGB</a>); <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a> (<a href="/wiki/WRC-TV" title="WRC-TV">WNBW</a>) and surrounding suburbs/environs. In <a href="/wiki/1948_World_Series" title="1948 World Series">1948</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-TVSignals_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TVSignals-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> games in <a href="/wiki/Boston" title="Boston">Boston</a> were only seen in the <a href="/wiki/Northeastern_United_States" title="Northeastern United States">Northeast</a>. Meanwhile, games in <a href="/wiki/Cleveland" title="Cleveland">Cleveland</a> were only seen in the <a href="/wiki/Midwestern_United_States" title="Midwestern United States">Midwest</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh" title="Pittsburgh">Pittsburgh</a>. The games were open to all channels with a network affiliation.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> In all, the 1948 World Series was televised to fans in seven Midwestern cities: Cleveland, <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">Chicago</a>, <a href="/wiki/Detroit" title="Detroit">Detroit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Milwaukee" title="Milwaukee">Milwaukee</a>, <a href="/wiki/St._Louis" title="St. Louis">St. Louis</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Toledo,_Ohio" title="Toledo, Ohio">Toledo</a>. By <a href="/wiki/1949_World_Series" title="1949 World Series">1949</a>, World Series games could now be seen east of the <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_River" title="Mississippi River">Mississippi River</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> The games were open to all channels with a network affiliation.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> By <a href="/wiki/1950_World_Series" title="1950 World Series">1950</a>, World Series games could be seen in most of the country,<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Wolters_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wolters-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Wolters_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wolters-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> but not all. <a href="/wiki/1951_World_Series" title="1951 World Series">1951</a> marked the first time that the World Series was televised <a href="/wiki/West_Coast_of_the_United_States" title="West Coast of the United States">coast</a><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> to <a href="/wiki/East_Coast_of_the_United_States" title="East Coast of the United States">coast</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-TVSignals_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TVSignals-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Meanwhile, <a href="/wiki/1955_World_Series" title="1955 World Series">1955</a> marked the first time that the World Series was <a href="/wiki/Television" title="Television">televised in color</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable Baseball.<br />\n</p><p><span id="cnote_**"><b><a href="#ref_**">^</a></b></span>&#160;<b>**:</b>&#160;Per the current <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_television_contracts" class="mw-redirect" title="Major League Baseball television contracts">broadcast agreement</a>, the World Series will be televised by Fox through 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><br />\n</p><p><span id="cnote_***"><b><a href="#ref_***">^</a></b></span>&#160;<b>***:</b>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Gillette_(brand)" class="mw-redirect" title="Gillette (brand)">Gillette</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> which sponsored World Series telecasts exclusively from roughly <a href="/wiki/1947_World_Series" title="1947 World Series">1947</a> to <a href="/wiki/1965_World_Series" title="1965 World Series">1965</a> (prior to <a href="/wiki/1966_World_Series" title="1966 World Series">1966</a>, the Series announcers were chosen by the Gillette Company along with the <a href="/wiki/Commissioner_of_Baseball" title="Commissioner of Baseball">Commissioner of Baseball</a> and <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">NBC</a>), paid for airtime on DuMont\'s <a href="/wiki/Owned-and-operated_television_stations_in_the_United_States" title="Owned-and-operated television stations in the United States">owned-and-operated</a> Pittsburgh affiliate, <a href="/wiki/KDKA-TV" title="KDKA-TV">WDTV</a> (now KDKA-TV) to air the World Series. In the meantime, Gillette also <a href="/wiki/Brokered_programming" title="Brokered programming">bought airtime</a> on <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_on_ABC" title="Major League Baseball on ABC">ABC</a>, <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_on_CBS" title="Major League Baseball on CBS">CBS</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_on_NBC" title="Major League Baseball on NBC">NBC</a>. More to the point, in some cities, the World Series was broadcast on three stations at once.<br />\n</p><p><span id="cnote_****"><b><a href="#ref_****">^</a></b></span>&#160;<b>****:</b>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_on_NBC" title="Major League Baseball on NBC">NBC</a> was originally scheduled to televise the entire <a href="/wiki/1995_World_Series" title="1995 World Series">1995 World Series</a>; however, due to the cancellation of the <a href="/wiki/1994_World_Series" title="1994 World Series">1994 Series</a> (which had been slated for <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_on_ABC" title="Major League Baseball on ABC">ABC</a>, who last televised a World Series in <a href="/wiki/1989_World_Series" title="1989 World Series">1989</a>), coverage ended up being split between the two networks. Game&#160;5 is, to date, the last Major League Baseball game to be telecast by ABC (had there been a Game&#160;7, ABC would\'ve televised it). This was the only World Series to be produced under the "<a href="/wiki/Baseball_Network" class="mw-redirect" title="Baseball Network">Baseball Network</a>" umbrella (a <a href="/wiki/Revenue_sharing" title="Revenue sharing">revenue sharing</a> <a href="/wiki/Joint_venture" title="Joint venture">joint venture</a> between Major League Baseball, ABC, and NBC). In July 1995, both networks announced that they would be pulling out of what was supposed to be a six-year-long  venture. NBC would next cover the <a href="/wiki/1997_World_Series" title="1997 World Series">1997</a> (NBC\'s first entirely since <a href="/wiki/1988_World_Series" title="1988 World Series">1988</a>) and <a href="/wiki/1999_World_Series" title="1999 World Series">1999 World Series</a> over the course of a five-year-long contract, in which <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_on_Fox" class="mw-redirect" title="Major League Baseball on Fox">Fox</a> would cover the World Series in even numbered years (<a href="/wiki/1996_World_Series" title="1996 World Series">1996</a>, <a href="/wiki/1998_World_Series" title="1998 World Series">1998</a>, and <a href="/wiki/2000_World_Series" title="2000 World Series">2000</a>).<br />\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_participation">International participation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: International participation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Baseball#Around-the-world" title="Baseball">Baseball \xc2\xa7&#160;Around-the-world</a>, and <a href="/wiki/History_of_baseball_outside_the_United_States" title="History of baseball outside the United States">History of baseball outside the United States</a></div>\n<p>Despite its name, the World Series remains solely the championship of the major-league baseball teams in the United States and Canada, although MLB, its players, and North American media sometimes informally refer to World Series winners as "world champions of baseball".<sup id="cite_ref-informal-quotes_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-informal-quotes-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The United States, Canada, and <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Mexican_League_(baseball)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mexican League (baseball)">Liga M\xc3\xa9xicana de B\xc3\xa9isbol</a></i>, established 1925) were the only professional baseball countries until a few decades into the 20th century. The first <a href="/wiki/Nippon_Professional_Baseball#History" title="Nippon Professional Baseball">Japanese professional baseball</a> efforts began in 1920. The current Japanese leagues date from the late 1940s (after World War II). Various Latin American leagues also formed around that time.\n</p><p>By the 1990s, baseball was played at a highly skilled level in many countries. Reaching North America\'s high-salary major leagues is the goal of many of the best players around the world, which gives a strong international flavor to the Series.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Many talented players from Latin America, the Caribbean, the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Rim" title="Pacific Rim">Pacific Rim</a>, and elsewhere now play in the majors. One notable exception is Cuban citizens, because of the <a href="/wiki/Cuba-United_States_relations" class="mw-redirect" title="Cuba-United States relations">political tensions between the US and Cuba</a> since 1959 (yet a number of Cuba\'s finest ballplayers have still managed to defect to the United States over the past half-century to play in the American professional leagues). Japanese professional players also have a difficult time coming to the North American leagues. They become free agents only after nine years playing service in the NPB, although their Japanese teams may at any time "<a href="/wiki/Posting_system" title="Posting system">post</a>" them for bids from MLB teams, which commonly happens at the player\'s request.\n</p><p>Several tournaments feature teams composed only of players from one country, similar to national teams in other sports. The <a href="/wiki/World_Baseball_Classic" title="World Baseball Classic">World Baseball Classic</a>, sponsored by Major League Baseball and sanctioned by the sport\'s world governing body, the <a href="/wiki/World_Baseball_Softball_Confederation" title="World Baseball Softball Confederation">World Baseball Softball Confederation</a> (WBSC), uses a format similar to the <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a> <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">World Cup</a> to promote competition between nations every four years. The WBSC has since added the <a href="/wiki/WBSC_Premier12" title="WBSC Premier12">Premier12</a>, a tournament also involving national teams; the first event was held in 2015, and is planned to be held every four years (in the middle of the World Baseball Classic cycle). The World Baseball Classic is held in March and the Premier12 is held in November, allowing both events to feature top-level players from all nations. The predecessor to the WBSC as the sport\'s international governing body, the <a href="/wiki/International_Baseball_Federation" title="International Baseball Federation">International Baseball Federation</a>, also sponsored a <a href="/wiki/Baseball_World_Cup" title="Baseball World Cup">Baseball World Cup</a> to crown a world champion. However, because the World Cup was held during the Northern Hemisphere summer, during the playing season of almost all top-level leagues, its teams did not feature the best talent from each nation. As a result, baseball fans paid little or no attention to the World Cup and generally disregarded its results. The <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Series" title="Caribbean Series">Caribbean Series</a> features competition among the league champions from Mexico, Puerto Rico, the Dominican Republic, and Venezuela but unlike the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_Club_World_Cup" title="FIFA Club World Cup">FIFA Club World Cup</a>, there is no club competition that features champions from all professional leagues across the world.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Image_gallery">Image gallery</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Image gallery">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul class="gallery
